Chapter on what is permissible to take as a pledge and what is not. [i.e., taking it as a pledge; i.e., taking the pledge with that thing] It is not valid to pledge a musha' (shared property), nor fruit on the palm tree without the tree, nor crops on the land without the land. It is not [i.e., pledging the fruit is not valid i.e., without the palm tree i.e., without the land]. Chapter on what is permissible to take as a pledge, etc. Since the author mentioned the preliminaries of the mortgagor's issues, he mentions in this chapter the details of what is valid to take as a pledge and what is not, because detail follows summary. He presented what is not valid first, in the style of non-ordered dissemination. (Fath) 'It is valid to pledge a musha'' means that pledging a musha' is not valid. Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between what is divisible and what is not. The author of al-'Inaya said: Pledging a musha' that is divisible and otherwise is invalid (fasid) according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible because the effect of the pledge according to him is the right to sell it, and a share is not prevented from sale. Our proof: the effect of the pledge is the establishment of the hand of use (yad al-istifa') and the right to continuous detention (habs da'im). Continuous detention in a musha' is inconceivable because it would nullify the arrangement (muha'ah) of possession, as if he pledged it one day and not the next. Therefore it is the same whether it is divisible or not, unlike a gift (hiba) which is permissible in something indivisible because its effect is ownership and ownership is not prevented by shuyu'. It is not valid from its partner either because establishing the hand of use in a musha' is inconceivable. If it were allowed, he would hold it one day by right of pledge and one day by right of ownership, thus he would be pledging it one day and not the next. This is unlike a lease (ijara) which is permissible in a musha' from the partner because its effect is enablement of usufruct, not detention, and the partner is capable of that. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) If shuyu' arises later, Abu Yusuf rules that the pledge remains valid, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) say it becomes invalid. This is like if the mortgagor authorizes a person to sell the pledged property at the due date, collectively or separately, and he sells part of it at the due date, according to Abu Yusuf the pledge is valid and is not invalidated by the occurrence of shuyu'. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq) Pledging a musha': Know that they differed on whether it is void (batil) or defective (fasid). Some said: void, no liability attaches. This statement is not correct. Some said: it is defective, not void, and what is taken possession of under a defective pledge is subject to liability. This is the correct view. What is taken under a void pledge is not subject to liability at all, because a void pledge is one that is not contracted at all, like a void sale. A defective one is contracted but with a defect, like a defective sale. The condition for the formation of a pledge is that it be property and that the counterpart is guaranteed, which is a condition for its validity. So wherever the pledge is property and the counterpart is guaranteed but some condition of validity is missing, the pledge is contracted but with the description of defectiveness. Wherever the pledge is not property or the counterpart is not guaranteed, the pledge is not contracted at all. (Fath) Al-musha': absolutely, whether the shuyu' is concurrent or subsequent. Fruit on palm tree, etc.: i.e., it is not valid to pledge fruit on the palm tree without the tree, nor to pledge crops on the land without the land, nor to pledge palm trees on the land without the land, because the pledged property is attached by creation to what is not pledged, so it is like a shared thing. Similarly, it is not valid to pledge land without palm trees because the pledge is occupied by what is not pledged, and it becomes like pledging land in which the mortgagor's property is located. Similarly, if he pledges land without a building, the pledge is occupied by the building. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that pledging land without trees is valid. ('Ayni, Fath) It is valid because...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on what is valid to take as a pledge. The ruling statement is: 'It is not valid to pledge a musha' (undivided share), nor fruit on the tree without the tree, nor crops without the land.' The commentary expands on three issues. First, the definition and ruling of pledging a musha': According to the Hanafi school, it is not valid, whether the share is divisible or not. The proof is that the pledge requires continuous detention (habs da'im), which is impossible in a shared property because one cannot detain it exclusively without a time-share arrangement, which is tantamount to 'pledging it one day and not the next'. This distinguishes the pledge from a gift (which requires ownership) and from a lease (which only requires enablement of usufruct). The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that the purpose is to sell upon default, and a share can be sold. The Hanafi rebuttal centers on the necessity of continuous detention. Second, there is an intra-madhhab dispute regarding the effect of subsequent shuyu' (turu' al-shuyu'): Abu Yusuf holds that the pledge remains valid if shuyu' arises later, while Muhammad (and Abu Hanifa according to some) holds it becomes invalid. Third, there is discussion on whether the contract is void (batil) or defective (fasid). The correct position is that it is fasid, not batil, because the elements of property and guarantee of the counterpart exist; only the condition of exclusive possession is missing. Consequently, if the mortgagee takes possession under a fasid contract, he is liable for the property. The passage ends with the parallel rulings on fruit, crops, and trees attached to land: they cannot be pledged independently due to inseparable attachment, which effectively creates a share in the whole. However, a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa allowed pledging land without trees.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-mushā‘): An undivided share in jointly owned property; a property that is shared without physical division.
الشيوع (al-shuyū‘): The state of being undivided and shared; the condition of ownership without partition.
الرهن الفاسد (al-rahn al-fāsid): A defective pledge: a contract that is concluded (mun'aqid) but has a deficiency in conditions other than the fundamental elements, such that possession still carries liability.
الرهن الباطل (al-rahn al-bāṭil): A void pledge: a contract that is not contracted at all, e.g., if the object is not property or the counterpart is not guaranteed.
الحبس الدائم (al-ḥabs al-dā'im): Continuous detention; the mortgagee's right to hold the pledged property until the debt is repaid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of taking possession under a fasid rahn contract (e.g., pledging a musha')?
A) No liability (daman) attaches to the mortgagee.
B) The mortgagee becomes the owner of the share.
C) The mortgagee is liable (daman) for the property.
D) The contract automatically becomes valid.

Key Takeaway
Pledging an undivided share (musha') is invalid in the Hanafi school because continuous detention cannot be achieved; the contract is fasid, not batil, and possession incurs liability.

Rahn — Pledge

What Can and Cannot Be Pledged in a Mortgage
Lists invalid pledges and condition of debt for valid mortgage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the invalid pledges (free persons, trusts, darak, sold item) and explain why a mortgage is valid only for a debt (including a promised debt) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A mortgage is valid only for a guaranteed debt; non-property and non-guaranteed items cannot be pledged.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lists several items that cannot be used as a pledge (rahn): free persons, trust properties, darak (seller's liability), and the sold item before delivery. It then establishes that a mortgage is only valid for a debt, even a future promised debt. Understanding these limitations is crucial for correctly forming a mortgage contract and avoiding void transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid pledges
List each item the matn declares invalid: free person (hurr), mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, trust amanahs, darak, and the sold item (mabee') before delivery.
The matn also prohibits a tree without its land, but the list focuses on non-property and non-guaranteed items.
2
Understand the rationale for each invalidity
For each invalid item, explain why it fails: free persons are not property; mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad have partial freedom and cannot be sold; trusts are not guaranteed; darak is not a present debt; sold item before delivery is not guaranteed (per the matn's initial ruling).
The commentary emphasizes the need for the pledged item to be 'madhmun' (guaranteed).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the sold item
Imam Muhammad holds that a mortgage with the sold item before delivery is fasid (defective) and the pledged item is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. This is the mufta bihi position, overriding the apparent ruling of the matn.
The commentator says 'al-mukhtar qawl Muhammad'.
4
Recognize the key condition: mortgage is only for a debt
The matn states 'Innama yasihhu bi daynin' – valid only for a debt. This includes an existing debt or a promised debt (maw'ud). The rationale is that mortgage is a means of satisfaction (istifa'), which requires an existing or imminent obligation.
The promised debt is treated as existing due to necessity and the default of a Muslim to fulfill promises.
5
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute on promised debt
The Hanafi position allowing mortgage for a promised debt is opposed by the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), who require an already existing debt. The Hanafi response relies on analogy (qiyas) with similar cases where non-existent is treated as existent (e.g., salam).
Thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis can take a pledge before the loan is given; others cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن
ما يجوز ارتمانه والارتمان به .
ونخل في أرض دونها، والحر والمدبر والمكاتب وأم الولد ولا بالأمانة وبالدرك أي دون الأرض وبالمبيع، وإنما يصح بدين، ولو موعودا،.
أي ولو كان الدين الاستحقاق، والحر والمدبر إلخ أي لا يصح رهن الحر والمدبر والمكاتب وكذا الوقف؛ لأنه لا يتحقق الاستيفاء من هؤلاء؛ لعدم المالية في الحر، وقيام المانع في الباقين (عيني رد المحتار) ولا بالأمانة: أي لا الرهن بالأمانات يصح كالوديعة والعارية والمضاربة، وبمال الشركة بأن أودع رجل عند رجل مالا، وأخذ منه رهنا، وقس على هذا، وجه عدم الصحة: أن قبض الرهن مضمون يضمنه المرتمن عند هلاكه فلابد من ضمان ما رهن به، ليقع القبض مضمونا، والأمانات ليست مضمونة، فلا يصح الرهن بها. وبالدرك: أي لا يصح الرهن بالدرك، وصورته : باع شيئا وسلمه إلى المشتري، فخاف المشتري من فأخذ بالثمن رهنا، فهذا الرهن باطل والكفالة به جائزة، والفرق أنه شرع للاستيفاء، ولا استيفاء إلا في الواجب، فلا يحتمل الإضافة، وأما الكفالة فتشبه ابتداء الالتزام بغير عوض، وذلك يحتملهما أي الإضافة والتعليق، كالتزام الصلاة والصوم رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٨/٢] وبالمبيع: أي إذا باع شيئا و لم يقبض المشتري المبيع، وأخذ المشتري من البائع رهنا لا يصح؛ لأن المبيع ليس بمضمون حتى إذا هلك المبيع لم يضمن البائع شيئا، ولكنه يسقط الثمن، وهو حق البائع ، كذا في "ملا مسكين"، قال في "الفتح": أقول: ما ذكره الشارح من أن المبيع ليس بمضمون، وجرى عليه في "الدرر" وغيرها يبتني على أن الرهن بالمبيع باطل، و به صرح عزمي زاده" عن "الكفاية" لكن نقل شيخنا عن "الاختيار " : أنه صرح بالفساد، وأنه مضمون بالأقل من قيمته ومن قيمة العين نقله عن نص محمد في "المبسوط" و"الجامع"، ثم قال: والمختار قول محمد، وجعل عدم ضمان الرهن بالمبيع قولا للقدوري في شرحه، ونقل فيه أن الفتوى على كونه فاسدا، وأنه مضمون بالأقل من قيمته وقيمة العين. وإنما يصح إلخ: أي لا يصح الرهن بغير الدين، وقد بينا المعنى فيه، وهو أن الرهن استيفاء، والاستيفاء يتحقق في الواجب، وهو الدين قوله : ولو" موعودا" أي يصح الرهن بالدين ولو كان الدين موعودا بأن يقول: أرهنتك هذا بألف لتقرضني ألفا مثلا، وقبض الرهن؛ لأن الموعود جعل كالموجود باعتبار الحاجة احتيالا للجواز؛ إذ لا يعطيه قبل قبض الرهن، فإن قيل: فليجعل المعدوم في الدرك موجودا للاشتراك في الحاجة؟ أجيب بأن المعدوم يجعل كالموجود إذا كان على شرف الوجود، والظاهر من حال المسلم انجاز وعده والدرك ليس كذلك؛ لأن الظاهر عدم الاستحقاق، فلو هلك الرهن في يده قبل أن يقرضه ألفا، فإنه يهلك مضمونا على المرتمن حتى يجب عليه تسليم الألف إلى الراهن بعد الهلاك إذا كان الموعود مساويا بقيمة الرهن، أو أقل منه.
يسم قدره، بأن
وأما إذا كان الدين الموعود أكثر من قيمته يجب على المرتمن الدفع بمقدار قيمة الرهن، وإن لم رهنه على أن يعطيه شيئا، فهلك في يده يعطي المرتمن الراهن؛ لأنه بالهلاك صار مستوفيا شيئا، فيكون بيانه إليه، ثم جواز الرهن بالدين الموعود مذهبنا، وعند الثلاثة لا يصح. (فتح، عيني، ملا مسكين)
The Book of Mortgage. What is permissible to be mortgaged and with what mortgage is taken. And (it is not valid to mortgage) a palm tree in land without it, and a free person, and a mudabbar, and a mukatab, and an umm walad, nor with a trust, nor with darak (i.e., without the land), and nor with the sold item. And it is only valid for a debt, even if promised. (Commentary:) Explanation of 'even if the debt is promised' ... (the commentary explains each invalid case and the proof).
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is from Kanz al-Daqaiq, a Hanafi matn, with commentary. It first lists items that cannot be used as a pledge: a tree without land (i.e., the tree is inseparable), free persons (they are not property), mudabbar and mukatab (they have partial freedom and cannot be sold to satisfy debt), umm walad (mother of child cannot be sold). Then it states that trust properties (like deposits, loans for use) cannot be pledged because the pledge must be guaranteed (madhmun), but trusts are not guaranteed. Darak (surety for defect) is also invalid, because the mortgage is for realizing a debt, and darak is not a guaranteed obligation. Similarly, the sold item before delivery cannot be pledged because it is not guaranteed (if it perishes, the seller does not owe compensation). However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that such a mortgage is valid but fasid (defective), and the pledged item is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. This is the mufta bihi. The passage then states that a mortgage is only valid for a debt, even a promised debt (e.g., 'I pledge this to you for a loan you will give me'). This is justified by necessity, as the promise is treated like an existing debt by way of legal stratagem. The Hanafi school allows this, while the three other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) do not.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt, held by the creditor.
الدرك (ad-darak): Liability for defects or legal claim against the seller; a form of guarantee.
الأمانة (al-amānah): Property held without liability for loss (e.g., deposit, loan for use).
مضمون (madhmun): Guaranteed, i.e., the holder is liable for loss or destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is explicitly stated as an invalid pledge?
A) A promised debt (dayn maw'ud)
B) A trust deposit (wadi'ah)
C) A mudabbar slave
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
A mortgage is valid only for a guaranteed debt; free persons, trusts, darak, and sold items cannot be validly pledged unless the latter is treated as fasid with guarantee per Imam Muhammad.

8 min
Pledge with Salam Capital and Currency Price
States validity of pledge for salam capital and sarf price with effect on contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pledging salam capital and currency price, and explain the effect of the pledge perishing or the parties separating before delivery.

Core Idea
A pledge for salam capital or currency price is valid; its destruction in the council completes the contract, but separation voids it.

The Hanafi school permits taking a pledge for the capital of a salam contract and for the price in a currency exchange. This lesson examines the validity conditions and the crucial effect of the pledge's destruction before the parties separate. We also explore the objection from Zafar, who considers it an invalid substitution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that a pledge can be taken for salam capital, the price in currency exchange (sarf), and the object of salam. If the pledge perishes in the council, it becomes as if the debt was satisfied. If the parties separate before that, the contract becomes void.
This applies only to the capital and price, not to the object of salam, as clarified in the commentary.
2
Understand the operative reasoning
The Hanafi position relies on the concept of istīfā' (satisfaction) through value, not specific item. Since the pledge covers the debt in terms of monetary value, its destruction in the council fulfills the requirement of delivery (qabḍ).
The proof is from the hadith or rational istihsan; the text cites the principle that the pledge's value is what matters.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Zafar (and some reports include Abu Yusuf) opposed the validity, arguing that the pledge amounts to an impermissible substitution. The Hanafi response is that the pledge is not a substitution but a security that, when destroyed, achieves satisfaction through value.
This is a classic qiyas khaafi vs. istihsan conflict.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a person pays 100 dirhams as salam capital and takes a pledge from the seller, and the pledge perishes in the assembly, the salam contract is complete. If they part before, the contract is void.
The same applies to the price in sarf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبرأس مال السلم، وثمن الصرف والمسلم فيه، فإن هلك صار مستوفيا، وللأب أن يرهن بدين عليه عبدا لطفله وصح رهن الحجرين والمكيل والموزون .
أي على الأب أي ولده الصغير الذهب والفضة كالحنطة والشعير كالحديد والصفر ولوصي كذلك
وبرأس مال السلم: أي يصح أخذ الرهن برأس مال السلم ومن الصرف والمسلم فيه، قال في "رد المحتار": وصورة هذه المسائل: أن يسلم مائة بطعام مثلا، أو يبيع دينارا بدرهم، ثم قبل القبض يدفع إلى المسلم إليه رهنا بالمائة، أو يأخذ رهنا بالدرهم أو بالطعام وصور بعضهم الأولى بأن يأخذ المسلم من المسلم إليه رهنا برأس المال الذي دفعه إليه، ويظهر لي أن الصواب ما صورته؛ لأنه إذا هلك الرهن في المجلس يصير المسلم مستردا لرأس المال، فكيف يقال: إن العقد يتم بذلك؟ وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل.
مطلقا،
قال العيني وقال :زفر: لا يجوز بناء على أن ذلك استبدال فإنه إذا هلك في مجلس العقد صار المرتمن مستوفيا، واستيفاء غير رأس المال فيها لا يصح ولنا أن المجانسة ثابتة من حيث المالية والمضمون من الرهن ماليته لا عينه، فيتحقق الاستيفاء من حيث المال، فصار كسائر الديون رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٨/٢] فإن هلك إلخ بيان لفائدة الرهن بالأشياء المذكورة، يعني إذا صح أخذ الرهن برأس المال وثمن الصرف، فإن هلك الرهن في مجلس العقد تم الصرف والسلم؛ لأنه لما أعطى المسلم المسلم إليه مائة برأس المال في السلم، أو أخذ رهنا بالدرهم في الصرف، وهلك الرهن في مجلس العقد صار المسلم إليه مستوفيا رأس ماله حكما، وكذا في الصرف؛ لوجود القبض واتحاد الجنس من حيث المالية، وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل الصرف والسلم؛ لفوات القبض حقيقة ،وحكما، هذا إذا كان الرهن برأس مال السلم أو ثمن الصرف، وأما إذا كان بالمسلم فيه فلا يبطله الافتراق قبل القبض؛ لأن قبضه لا يجب في المجلس، ولهذا قال في رد المحتار": أفاد القهستاني: أن المراد هلك الرهن برأس المال أو بثمن الصرف دون المسلم فيه؛ لمنافاته لقوله: "وإن افترقا"؛ لأن السلم يصح أقول: ولهذا ذكر في "الدرر" مسألة المسلم فيه مؤخرة. فافهم واحفظ. وللأب أن يرهن إلخ: أي يجوز للأب أن يرهن عبدا لطفله بدين عليه أي على الأب؛ لأنه يملك إيداعه، وهذا نظر منه في حق الصبي؛ لأنه إذا هلك يهلك مضمونا، والوديعة أمانة والوصي في هذا كالأب، وعن أبي يوسف وزفر أنهما لا يملكان؛ لأن الرهن إيفاء حكما فلا يملكانه كالإيفاء حقيقة وهذا هو القياس، وجه الاستحسان: أن في حقيقة الإيفاء إزالة ملك الصغير من غير عوض يقابله في الحال، وفي الرهن نصب حافظ لمال صغير في المال مع بقاء ملكه، فافترقا، ثم إذا جاز الرهن يصير المرتمن مستوفيا دينه عند هلاكه حكما، ويصير الأب والوصي موفيا له به، ويضمنان ذلك القدر للصغير، ولو رهن الأب متاع الصغير، فأدرك الابن، ومات الأب، فليس له أن يسترده حتى يقضي الدين؛ لأن تصرف الأب عليه نافذ لازم. (عيني، فتح) صح رهن الحجرين إلخ: وإنما جاز رهن هذه الأشياء؛ لإمكان الاستيفاء منها، فكانت محلا .للرهن تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٩٧/٨]
And with the capital of salam, and the price of currency exchange and the object of salam; if it perishes, it becomes realized. And for a father, he may pledge a slave of his child for a debt upon him. And the pledge of gold and silver and measured and weighed items is valid. (Commentary:) ...
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage continues from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It states three rulings: (1) A pledge can be taken for the capital of a salam contract, for the price in a currency exchange (sarf), and for the object of salam (the commodity to be delivered). If the pledge perishes in the council, the contract is completed as if delivery occurred. However, if they separate before the pledge perishes, the contract becomes void. There is a dispute with Zafar who says it is invalid because it is like substitution, but the Hanafi view is that oneness of value suffices. (2) A father (and similarly an executor) may pledge a slave belonging to his minor child for a debt owed by the father. This is by istihsan (juristic preference) because the debt is secured and the child's property is protected. Abu Yusuf and Zafar oppose based on qiyas (analogy to direct payment), but the Hanafi view is that the father acts as guardian. If the father dies, the child cannot reclaim the slave until the debt is paid. (3) Pledging gold, silver, and measured/weighed items (like wheat, barley, iron, brass) is valid because they can be used for satisfaction of debt.

Key Terms
برأس مال السلم (bi ra's māl as-salam): The capital given in a salam contract (forward sale).
الاستيفاء (al-istīfā'): Satisfaction or receipt of the debt or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, if a pledge is taken for the capital and the parties separate before the pledge perishes, what is the ruling?
A) The salam contract becomes void
B) The pledge must be returned and the contract continues
C) The contract is complete if the pledge is later destroyed
D) The contract is void only if the pledge perishes

Key Takeaway
A pledge for salam capital or currency price is valid; its destruction in the contract council completes the forward sale or exchange, but separation before destruction voids it.

Father's Pledge of Child's Property
States validity of father's pledge of child's property with istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father's pledge of his minor child's property for his own debt, and explain the istihsan reasoning that makes it valid.

Core Idea
A father may pledge his minor child's property for his own debt by istihsan, protecting the child's assets while securing the debt.

The matn states that a father can pledge a slave belonging to his child for a debt incumbent upon the father. This lesson delves into the dispute with Abu Yusuf and Zafar, who opposed it based on qiyas, and the Hanafi preference for istihsan. We also examine the consequences when the father dies and the child's right to reclaim the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn declares that a father (and similarly an executor) may pledge a slave (or any property) of his minor child for a debt that the father himself owes. This is a special dispensation for the father due to his guardianship.
The ruling is specific to the father (and executor); it does not extend to other relatives.
2
Understand the opponents' qiyas
Abu Yusuf and Zafar argue that the father cannot pledge the child's property because a pledge is a form of constructive payment (īfā' ḥukmī). Since the father cannot directly pay his debt from the child's property without compensation, he cannot indirectly do so through a pledge.
This is a strict analogy (qiyas jali).
3
Learn the Hanafi istihsan reasoning
The Hanafi school prefers istihsan: the pledge is not a payment but a security. The child's property is better protected because it remains with the father as a pledge, whereas if the father were to directly pay the debt by selling the child's property (which he cannot), the child would lose ownership. The pledge keeps the property secure while the debt is outstanding.
The key is that the pledge preserves the child's ownership; it is a safeguarding measure.
4
Analyze the consequences
If the father dies, the child cannot reclaim the pledged property until the debt is paid. The father's transaction is binding (lāzim). If the pledge perishes, the father or executor is liable to compensate the child.
This ensures that the father's pledge is effective and protects the creditor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway

Validity of Pledging Gold, Silver, and Measured/Weighed Items
States validity of pledge for gold, silver, and measured/weighed items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school validates the pledge of gold, silver, and all measured/weighed items, and explain the rationale that such items can be used for satisfaction of debt.

Core Idea
Any item that can satisfy a debt – like gold, silver, and measured or weighed goods – is a valid object of pledge.

The matn concludes with a brief but important ruling: the pledge of 'the two stones' (gold and silver) and items that are measured (makīl) or weighed (mawzūn) is valid. This lesson explains the underlying principle: these items are suitable for satisfying debts because they are fungible and can be valued equally, making them secure pledges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items mentioned
The matn lists: al-ḥajarayn (literally 'the two stones', meaning gold and silver), al-makīl (measured by volume, like wheat), and al-mawzūn (weighed, like iron). These categories cover most fungible goods.
The commentary extends to items like copper and brass, which are also weighed.
2
Understand the underlying rationale
The pledge is valid because these items can be used to satisfy the debt. The key condition for a valid object of pledge is that it can fulfill the debt if the pledge is forfeited. Gold, silver, and measured/weighed items are easily valued and can serve as payment.
This is a general principle: any property that can be sold to pay off a debt can be pledged.
3
Contrast with items that cannot be pledged
Items that are not measurable or weighable, or that are perishable or not fungible, may not be valid objects of pledge because they cannot reliably satisfy the debt upon default.
The Hanafi school has detailed conditions for the pledged object; this lesson focuses on the positive ruling for these categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبرأس مال السلم، وثمن الصرف والمسلم فيه، فإن هلك صار مستوفيا، وللأب أن يرهن بدين عليه عبدا لطفله وصح رهن الحجرين والمكيل والموزون .
أي على الأب أي ولده الصغير الذهب والفضة كالحنطة والشعير كالحديد والصفر ولوصي كذلك
وبرأس مال السلم: أي يصح أخذ الرهن برأس مال السلم ومن الصرف والمسلم فيه، قال في "رد المحتار": وصورة هذه المسائل: أن يسلم مائة بطعام مثلا، أو يبيع دينارا بدرهم، ثم قبل القبض يدفع إلى المسلم إليه رهنا بالمائة، أو يأخذ رهنا بالدرهم أو بالطعام وصور بعضهم الأولى بأن يأخذ المسلم من المسلم إليه رهنا برأس المال الذي دفعه إليه، ويظهر لي أن الصواب ما صورته؛ لأنه إذا هلك الرهن في المجلس يصير المسلم مستردا لرأس المال، فكيف يقال: إن العقد يتم بذلك؟ وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل.
مطلقا،
قال العيني وقال :زفر: لا يجوز بناء على أن ذلك استبدال فإنه إذا هلك في مجلس العقد صار المرتمن مستوفيا، واستيفاء غير رأس المال فيها لا يصح ولنا أن المجانسة ثابتة من حيث المالية والمضمون من الرهن ماليته لا عينه، فيتحقق الاستيفاء من حيث المال، فصار كسائر الديون رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٨/٢] فإن هلك إلخ بيان لفائدة الرهن بالأشياء المذكورة، يعني إذا صح أخذ الرهن برأس المال وثمن الصرف، فإن هلك الرهن في مجلس العقد تم الصرف والسلم؛ لأنه لما أعطى المسلم المسلم إليه مائة برأس المال في السلم، أو أخذ رهنا بالدرهم في الصرف، وهلك الرهن في مجلس العقد صار المسلم إليه مستوفيا رأس ماله حكما، وكذا في الصرف؛ لوجود القبض واتحاد الجنس من حيث المالية، وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل الصرف والسلم؛ لفوات القبض حقيقة ،وحكما، هذا إذا كان الرهن برأس مال السلم أو ثمن الصرف، وأما إذا كان بالمسلم فيه فلا يبطله الافتراق قبل القبض؛ لأن قبضه لا يجب في المجلس، ولهذا قال في رد المحتار": أفاد القهستاني: أن المراد هلك الرهن برأس المال أو بثمن الصرف دون المسلم فيه؛ لمنافاته لقوله: "وإن افترقا"؛ لأن السلم يصح أقول: ولهذا ذكر في "الدرر" مسألة المسلم فيه مؤخرة. فافهم واحفظ. وللأب أن يرهن إلخ: أي يجوز للأب أن يرهن عبدا لطفله بدين عليه أي على الأب؛ لأنه يملك إيداعه، وهذا نظر منه في حق الصبي؛ لأنه إذا هلك يهلك مضمونا، والوديعة أمانة والوصي في هذا كالأب، وعن أبي يوسف وزفر أنهما لا يملكان؛ لأن الرهن إيفاء حكما فلا يملكانه كالإيفاء حقيقة وهذا هو القياس، وجه الاستحسان: أن في حقيقة الإيفاء إزالة ملك الصغير من غير عوض يقابله في الحال، وفي الرهن نصب حافظ لمال صغير في المال مع بقاء ملكه، فافترقا، ثم إذا جاز الرهن يصير المرتمن مستوفيا دينه عند هلاكه حكما، ويصير الأب والوصي موفيا له به، ويضمنان ذلك القدر للصغير، ولو رهن الأب متاع الصغير، فأدرك الابن، ومات الأب، فليس له أن يسترده حتى يقضي الدين؛ لأن تصرف الأب عليه نافذ لازم. (عيني، فتح) صح رهن الحجرين إلخ: وإنما جاز رهن هذه الأشياء؛ لإمكان الاستيفاء منها، فكانت محلا .للرهن تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٩٧/٨]
And with the capital of salam, and the price of currency exchange and the object of salam; if it perishes, it becomes realized. And for a father, he may pledge a slave of his child for a debt upon him. And the pledge of gold and silver and measured and weighed items is valid. (Commentary:) ...
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage continues from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It states three rulings: (1) A pledge can be taken for the capital of a salam contract, for the price in a currency exchange (sarf), and for the object of salam (the commodity to be delivered). If the pledge perishes in the council, the contract is completed as if delivery occurred. However, if they separate before the pledge perishes, the contract becomes void. There is a dispute with Zafar who says it is invalid because it is like substitution, but the Hanafi view is that oneness of value suffices. (2) A father (and similarly an executor) may pledge a slave belonging to his minor child for a debt owed by the father. This is by istihsan (juristic preference) because the debt is secured and the child's property is protected. Abu Yusuf and Zafar oppose based on qiyas (analogy to direct payment), but the Hanafi view is that the father acts as guardian. If the father dies, the child cannot reclaim the slave until the debt is paid. (3) Pledging gold, silver, and measured/weighed items (like wheat, barley, iron, brass) is valid because they can be used for satisfaction of debt.

Key Terms
الحجرين (al-ḥajarayn): The two stones: gold and silver.
المكيل (al-makīl): Measured by volume, e.g., wheat, barley.
الموزون (al-mawzūn): Weighed, e.g., iron, brass, gold, silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the pledge of measured and weighed items valid?
A) Because they are valuable and rare
B) Because they can be used to satisfy the debt
C) Because they are heavy and secure
D) Because the law specifically lists them

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits pledging gold, silver, and any measured or weighed items because they are fungible and can satisfy a debt upon default.

Pledging with Salam Capital and Sarf Price
Ruling on validity and effect of destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pledging with salam capital and sarf price, explain the effect of destruction in the contract session, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Zufar.

Core Idea
A pledge destroyed in the contract session deems receipt of value, completing the salam/sarf by istihsan.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary addresses a subtle intersection of rahn, salam, and sarf. When a pledge is given for the capital of salam or the price of sarf, its destruction in the same session creates a deemed receipt (istifa'), completing the contract. This ruling relies on istihsan based on monetary value congruence. Zufar's opposing view challenges this as an invalid substitution. Understanding this helps grasp how Hanafi fiqh uses constructive receipt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts involved
Salam (forward sale) and sarf (currency exchange) both require immediate receipt (qabd) of the price in the session. Here, a pledge is given instead of actual receipt.
The pledge serves as a substitute for the capital/price.
2
State the ruling on validity
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) holds it valid to take a pledge for the capital of salam and the price of sarf. This is based on istihsan.
Zufar considers it invalid as a substitution (istibdal).
3
Understand the effect of destruction
If the pledge is destroyed in the contract session, the creditor is deemed to have received the capital/price (istifa'), completing the contract.
Destruction in the session suffices for constructive receipt.
4
Analyze Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that receiving something other than the actual capital is invalid; it is a substitution. The Hanafi response: the pledge's monetary value (maliyyah) is congruent, not its substance.
The dispute is over the nature of receipt: substance vs. value.
5
Recognize the distinction for muslam fihi
If the pledge is for the muslam fihi (the item to be delivered in salam), separation before qabd does not void the contract because immediate qabd is not required for the delivery item.
This nuance is emphasized in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبرأس مال السلم، وثمن الصرف والمسلم فيه، فإن هلك صار مستوفيا، قال في "رد المحتار": وصورة هذه المسائل: أن يسلم مائة بطعام مثلا، أو يبيع دينارا بدرهم، ثم قبل القبض يدفع إلى المسلم إليه رهنا بالمائة، أو يأخذ رهنا بالدرهم أو بالطعام وصور بعضهم الأولى بأن يأخذ المسلم من المسلم إليه رهنا برأس المال الذي دفعه إليه، ويظهر لي أن الصواب ما صورته؛ لأنه إذا هلك الرهن في المجلس يصير المسلم مستردا لرأس المال، فكيف يقال: إن العقد يتم بذلك؟ وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل. قال العيني وقال :زفر: لا يجوز بناء على أن ذلك استبدال فإنه إذا هلك في مجلس العقد صار المرتمن مستوفيا، واستيفاء غير رأس المال فيها لا يصح ولنا أن المجانسة ثابتة من حيث المالية والمضمون من الرهن ماليته لا عينه، فيتحقق الاستيفاء من حيث المال، فصار كسائر الديون رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٨/٢] فإن هلك إلخ بيان لفائدة الرهن بالأشياء المذكورة، يعني إذا صح أخذ الرهن برأس المال وثمن الصرف، فإن هلك الرهن في مجلس العقد تم الصرف والسلم؛ لأنه لما أعطى المسلم المسلم إليه مائة برأس المال في السلم، أو أخذ رهنا بالدرهم في الصرف، وهلك الرهن في مجلس العقد صار المسلم إليه مستوفيا رأس ماله حكما، وكذا في الصرف؛ لوجود القبض واتحاد الجنس من حيث المالية، وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل الصرف والسلم؛ لفوات القبض حقيقة ،وحكما، هذا إذا كان الرهن برأس مال السلم أو ثمن الصرف، وأما إذا كان بالمسلم فيه فلا يبطله الافتراق قبل القبض؛ لأن قبضه لا يجب في المجلس، ولهذا قال في رد المحتار": أفاد القهستاني: أن المراد هلك الرهن برأس المال أو بثمن الصرف دون المسلم فيه؛ لمنافاته لقوله: "وإن افترقا"؛ لأن السلم يصح أقول: ولهذا ذكر في "الدرر" مسألة المسلم فيه مؤخرة. فافهم واحفظ.
And with the capital of salam, and the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi, and if it is destroyed, the mortgagee becomes the recipient (mustawfi). He said in Radd al-Muhtar: The form of these issues is: that one makes a salam of one hundred for food, for example, or sells a dinar for a dirham, then before receipt (qabd) he gives the muslam ilayhi a pledge for the one hundred, or takes a pledge for the dirham or the food. And some depicted the first as the muslim taking from the muslam ilayhi a pledge for the capital that he paid him. It appears to me that the correct is what he depicted; because if the pledge is destroyed in the session, the muslim would be reclaiming the capital, so how is it said that the contract is completed by that? And if they separate before destruction, it is void. Al-Ayni said: And Zufar said: It is not permissible, on the basis that this is a substitution; because if it is destroyed in the contract session, the mortgagee becomes a recipient (mustawfi), and receiving other than the capital in it (salam/sarf) is not valid. Our proof: that the congruence (mujanasah) is established in terms of monetary value (maliyyah), and the warrant (madmun) of the pledge is its monetary value, not its substance, so receipt is realized in terms of value, so it becomes like other debts. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 2/408). "Then if it is destroyed" etc. is an explanation of the benefit of pledging with the mentioned things; meaning if the pledge is valid with the capital and the price of sarf, then if the pledge is destroyed in the contract session, the sarf and salam are completed; because when the muslim gave the muslam ilayhi one hundred as capital in salam, or took a pledge for the dirham in sarf, and the pledge was destroyed in the contract session, the muslam ilayhi is deemed to have received his capital, and likewise in sarf; due to the existence of qabd and unity of genus in terms of monetary value. And if they separate before destruction, the sarf and salam are void due to the lack of qabd in reality and in effect. This is when the pledge is for the capital of salam or the price of sarf. But if it is for the muslam fihi, separation before qabd does not void it, because its qabd is not obligatory in the session. For this reason, he said in Radd al-Muhtar: Al-Qahistani said that the meaning is the destruction of the pledge for the capital or the price of sarf, not for the muslam fihi, because it contradicts his statement "and if they separate"; because salam is valid. I (the commentator) say: for this reason, in al-Durar, the issue of muslam fihi is mentioned later. So understand and memorize.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar) on the validity of pledging with salam capital and the price of sarf. The matn states that it is permissible to take a pledge for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi (the item to be delivered in salam). If the pledge is destroyed in the contract session, the mortgagee is considered to have received his due (istifa'). The commentary clarifies the scenarios: for example, if a person gives a loan of 100 in salam for food, or sells a dinar for a dirham (sarf), then before the actual handover, the debtor gives a pledge. If the pledge is destroyed in the same session, the contract is complete because the creditor is deemed to have received the capital. Zufar disagrees, arguing that this is a kind of substitution (istibdal) and that receiving something other than the actual capital is invalid. The Hanafi position (our school) relies on istihsan: the pledge's value is congruent in terms of monetary value (maliyyah), not its specific substance, so it is like other debts. A crucial distinction: if the pledge is for the muslam fihi (the item to be delivered), separation before receipt does not invalidate the contract because receipt is not required immediately. The author emphasizes understanding and memorizing this subtle point.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for future delivery of fungible goods.
صرف (sarf): Exchange of gold, silver, or currency; immediate delivery (qabd) is required in the session.
قبض (qabd): Physical or legal taking of possession; necessary for completion of certain contracts.
استيفاء (istifa'): Receiving or collecting what is due, here deemed fulfillment of debt through pledge destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what happens if a pledge given for the capital of salam is destroyed in the contract session?
A) The salam contract becomes void.
B) The salam contract is completed and the creditor is deemed to have received the capital.
C) The creditor must return the pledge's value.
D) The contract is suspended until replacement.

Key Takeaway
Pledging with salam capital or sarf price is valid per Hanafi; destruction in the session deems receipt of value, completing the contract by istihsan.

Father's Authority to Pledge Child's Property for His Debt
Intra-Hanafi dispute with istihsan-based ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father may pledge his minor child’s property for his own debt, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf/Zufar, and apply the distinction between actual payment (ifa’ haqiqi) and constructive payment (ifa’ hukmi) that underpins the istihsan argument.

Core Idea
A father may pledge his child’s property because it preserves ownership while securing the debt, unlike direct payment.

This lesson examines the father’s authority to use his minor child’s property as collateral for his own debt. The Hanafi school, based on istihsan, permits this as a protective measure for the child’s welfare, even though analogy (qiyas) would forbid it. We will explore the proofs and the intra-Hanafi disagreement, focusing on the distinction between actual and constructive payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is in question and what the Hanafi ruling is. The act is a father pledging his minor child’s property for a debt owed by the father. The ruling is that it is valid (ja’iz).
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the evidence the Hanafi school uses to support the validity. The text mentions the father’s authority to deposit the child’s property (wadi’ah) as a basis, implying that the pledge is a type of deposit or guarantee that protects the child’s interest.
The proof is istihsan, which overrides the apparent qiyas.
3
Analyze the qiyas objection
Examine the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Zufar that the pledge is invalid. They analogize the pledge to an actual payment (ifa’ haqiqi) of the child’s property for the father’s debt, which would be prohibited because it removes ownership without compensation.
Their qiyas is based on the principle that the father cannot give away the child’s property without immediate countervalue.
4
Examine the istihsan response
Understand how the Hanafi response distinguishes the pledge from actual payment. In a pledge, the child’s ownership remains intact; the property is merely a security. If destroyed, the creditor’s debt is deemed paid (ifa’ hukmi), and the father must compensate the child. This preserves the child’s immediate interest.
The key distinction is that ownership is not transferred at the time of pledge.
5
Determine the practical consequences
Trace what happens after the pledge is made and if the property is destroyed or the father dies. The father becomes a deemed payer, and the child cannot reclaim the pledged property until the debt is paid, because the father’s transaction is binding.
This shows that the ruling has real-world effects on the child’s rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللأب أن يرهن بدين عليه عبدا لطفله أي على الأب أي ولده الصغير الذهب والفضة كالحنطة والشعير كالحديد والصفر ولوصي كذلك قال في "فتح القدير": أي يجوز للأب أن يرهن عبدا لطفله بدين عليه أي على الأب؛ لأنه يملك إيداعه، وهذا نظر منه في حق الصبي؛ لأنه إذا هلك يهلك مضمونا، والوديعة أمانة والوصي في هذا كالأب، وعن أبي يوسف وزفر أنهما لا يملكان؛ لأن الرهن إيفاء حكما فلا يملكانه كالإيفاء حقيقة وهذا هو القياس، وجه الاستحسان: أن في حقيقة الإيفاء إزالة ملك الصغير من غير عوض يقابله في الحال، وفي الرهن نصب حافظ لمال صغير في المال مع بقاء ملكه، فافترقا، ثم إذا جاز الرهن يصير المرتمن مستوفيا دينه عند هلاكه حكما، ويصير الأب والوصي موفيا له به، ويضمنان ذلك القدر للصغير، ولو رهن الأب متاع الصغير، فأدرك الابن، ومات الأب، فليس له أن يسترده حتى يقضي الدين؛ لأن تصرف الأب عليه نافذ لازم.
And for the father is that he may pledge a slave of his child for a debt owed by him (the father), meaning upon the father, meaning his young child - gold and silver like wheat and barley, like iron and brass - and similarly for the executor. He said in Fath al-Qadir: That is, it is permissible for the father to pledge a slave of his child for a debt owed by him (the father), because he has the authority to deposit it. This is a consideration for the welfare of the minor; because if it is destroyed, it is destroyed as a warranted item, whereas a deposit is a trust. And the executor is like the father in this. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf and Zufar that they do not have this authority, because a pledge is a constructive payment, so they do not own it just as they do not own actual payment, and this is the qiyas. The istihsan argument: that in actual payment, the minor's ownership is removed without an immediate countervalue, whereas in pledge, a protector is set up for the minor's property while his ownership remains, so they differ. Then if the pledge is permissible, the mortgagee becomes deemed recipient of his debt upon destruction, and the father/executor becomes deemed payer, and they must compensate the minor for that amount. If the father pledged the minor's goods, then the son reached maturity, and the father died, the son may not reclaim them until he pays the debt, because the father's action is binding and effective.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a father's (or guardian's) authority to pledge the property of his minor child to secure his own debt. The matn states that a father may pledge a slave of his child for a debt he owes, and similarly a guardian (wasi) may do so. The commentary explains that the father has this authority because he can deposit the property, and this is seen as a precautionary measure for the child's benefit: if the pledge is destroyed, it is lost under a guarantee (madmun), whereas a deposit would be lost as a trust (amanah). Abu Yusuf and Zufar disagree, saying the father does not have this authority because pledging is like constructive payment (ifa' hukman), and just as he cannot actually pay with the child's property, he cannot do so constructively. This is the qiyas. The Hanafi response (istihsan) distinguishes: in actual payment, the child's ownership is removed without immediate compensation, but in pledge, the ownership remains and the property serves as security. Thus, if the pledge is destroyed, the creditor's debt is deemed paid, and the father/guardian must compensate the child. Moreover, if the father pledged the child's property and then the father dies, the child cannot repossess the pledged property until the debt is paid, because the father's transaction is valid and binding.

Key Terms
إيفاء (ifa'): Payment or settlement of a debt; here constructive payment through pledge.
وديعة (wadi'ah): Deposit; property given for safekeeping without guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, if a father pledges his minor child's property for his own debt and it is destroyed, what happens?
A) The child suffers the loss with no compensation.
B) The father must compensate the child for the value of the property.
C) The pledge is invalid and the debt remains.
D) The creditor loses his right to the debt.

Key Takeaway
The father may pledge his minor child's property for his own debt, but he must compensate the child if the property is destroyed.

Pledging Weighed/Measured Items and Conditional Pledge in Sale
Rulings on pledging weighed/measured items and conditional pledge in sale with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the validity of pledging weighed/measured items and apply the ruling on conditional pledges in sale, including the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on destruction of similar-genus pledges.

Core Idea
Pledging weighed/measured items is valid; a conditional pledge in sale is valid by istihsan, but the buyer is not compelled to fulfil it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes two important rulings in Hanafi fiqh: the validity of pledging items that are measured or weighed, and the effect of a condition in a sale that requires the buyer to give a specific pledge. While the general principle (qiyas) would invalidate such a condition, the Hanafi school applies istihsan to uphold it for the purpose of security. Additionally, an intra-madhhab disagreement arises when similar pledged items are destroyed: does the debt discharge by weight or value? Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly structuring sale-and-pledge transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal acts are being ruled upon: (1) pledge of heavy stones, mikyal, and mawzun items; (2) a sale conditioned on the buyer giving a specific pledge. For each, state the hukm (sahih/valid).
The passage opens with 'صح رهن الحجرين والمكيل والموزون' and later addresses the conditional pledge.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
For the conditional pledge, the text invokes istihsan as the proof, overriding the qiyas that would invalidate the condition. Identify the specific reasoning (suitability for contract purpose).
Istihsan is a secondary source in Hanafi usul, used here to achieve equity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof leads to the ruling. Istihsan considers the condition 'munasib' (suitable) because security naturally attaches to the price obligation. The qiyas argument is that the condition is not required by the contract and provides benefit to one party.
The text contrasts qiyas with istihsan explicitly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Two intra-Hanafi disagreements: (a) Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn on destruction of similar-genus pledged items: weight vs value from a different genus; (b) Zufar vs the majority on compelling the buyer to fulfil the conditional pledge.
Each ikhtilaf has a practical consequence (thamarah).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text does not explicitly tarjih between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, but later authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view to avoid harm. On the buyer's compulsion, the majority view (not compelled) is upheld.
The mufta bihi for destruction often follows the Sahibayn; for conditional pledge, the Hanafi fatwa is that the buyer is not compelled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح رهن الحجرين والمكيل والموزون . أي على الأب أي ولده الصغير الذهب والفضة كالحنطة والشعير كالحديد والصفر قال في "فتح القدير": صح رهن الحجرين إلخ: وإنما جاز رهن هذه الأشياء؛ لإمكان الاستيفاء منها، فكانت محلا للرهن. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٩٧/٨] فإن رهنت بجنسها هلكت من الدين، ولا عبرة بالجودة، ومن باع عبدا على أن يرهن المشتري بالثمن شيئا بعينه فامتنع لم يجبر، وللبائع فسخ البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالا أو قيمة الرهن رهنا، وإن قال للبائع أمسك هذا الثوب رهنا جاز استحسانا . هلكت من الدين إلخ: يعني إذا رهنت هذه الأشياء بجنسها، وهلكت عند المرتمن هلكت بمثلها من الدين وزنا أو كيلا لا قيمة، سواء كانت قيمة هذه الأشياء كوزنها أو لا، ولا عبرة بالجودة؛ لأنها ساقطة الاعتبار عند المقابلة بالجنس، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة؛ فإن عنده يصير مستوفيا باعتبار الوزن دون القيمة، وعندهما: يضمن القيمة من خلاف الجنس، فتكون رهنا مكانه ويملك المرتمن الهالك بالضمان بيانه إذا رهن الراهن فضة وزنه عشرة بعشرة دراهم وهلك الفضة فإن كانت قيمته مثل وزن عشرة، يسقط الدين بالاتفاق، وإن كانت قيمته أقل من وزنه بأن كانت قيمة الفضة ثمانية مثلا، أو كانت قيمته أكثر من عشرة بأن كانت اثنى عشرة درهما، فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم اعتبار صفة الجودة. وعندهما: يضمن المرتمن قيمته من خلاف جنسه؛ لأنه لو اعتبر الوزن وحده من غير اعتبار صفة جودة أو رداءة، وأسقط القيمة، لزم الإضرار بأحدهما يعني بالمرتمن إذا كانت أقل من وزنه، وبالراهن فيما إذا كانت القيمة أكثر، ولو اعتبر القيمة وجعل مستوفيا باعتبارها أدى إلى الربا، فتعين ما ذكر من أنه يضمن قيمته من خلاف، ثم عند الإمام: إن تساويا الدين والرهن في الوزن فظاهر وإن كان الدين أزيد فالزائد في ذمة الراهن، وإن كان الرهن أزيد فالزائد أمانة ولو رهن هذه الأشياء بخلاف جنسها ،فهلكت هلكت بقيمتها كسائر الأموال وهو ظاهر، هذا حاصل ما في "العيني والفتح وغيرهما"، فاحفظه. على أن. يرهن المشتري إلخ: يعني من باع عبدا على هذا الشرط المذكور جاز البيع استحسانا، والقياس أن لا يجوز؛ لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وفيه نفع لأحد المتعاقدين، ولأنه صفقة في صفقة، وهو منهي عنه، وجه الاستحسان أنه شرط ملائم للعقد؛ لأن الكفالة والرهن للاستيثاق، وهو يلائم وجوب الثمن، فإذا كان الرهن معينا اعتبر معنى الشرط وهو الاستيثاق، فصح العقد، وإلا اعتبر عين الشرط ففسد. (فتح) فامتنع إلخ: أي إذا جاز البيع هذا الشرط، وامتنع بعد ذلك المشتري عن الرهن لا يجبر، وقال زفر: يجبر؛ لأنه بالشرط صار حقا من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في عقد الرهن وجوابه أن عقد الرهن تبرع كإعطاء الكفيل، جبر على المتبرع، وإنما يصير حقا من حقوقه إذا وجد، ولم يوجد بعد البيع والوعد بالرهن لا يكون فوق الرهن، ولو رهنه لا يلزم ما لم يسلم، فلأن لا يصير لازما بالوعد أولى. (فتح) وللبائع فسخ البيع إلخ: يعني لا يجبر المشتري على الرهن ولكن للبائع فسخ البيع؛ لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه، وفواته يوجب الخيار، إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالا، فحينئذ ليس للبائع خيار الفسخ؛ لحصول المقصود، أو يدفع قيمة الرهن المشروط رهنا؛ لأن المقصود من الرهن المشروط يحصل بالقيمة. (فتح، عيني)
The pledge of the two heavy stones (gold and silver) and what is measured and weighed is valid. That is, upon the father and his young child - gold and silver like wheat and barley, like iron and brass. He said in Fath al-Qadir: the pledge of the two heavy stones etc. is valid: it is permissible to pledge these things because it is possible to recover value from them, so they are a locus for a pledge. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/497). Then if similar items are pledged, they are destroyed against the debt, and quality is not considered. Whoever sells a slave on the condition that the buyer pledge a specific item for the price, and the buyer refuses, he is not compelled. But the seller may rescind the sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately or gives the equivalent value as a pledge. And if he says to the seller 'Hold this garment as a pledge', it is valid by istihsan. "Destroyed against the debt" etc. means if these items are pledged with similar items, and they are destroyed with the mortgagee, they are destroyed by their equivalent from the debt by weight or measure, not by value, whether the value equals the weight or not. Quality is not considered because it is irrelevant when comparing by genus. This is according to Abu Hanifa; with him, the mortgagee is considered to have received by weight not value. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees the value from a different genus, so that becomes a pledge in its place, and he owns the destroyed item by guarantee. Explanation: if the pledgor pledges silver weighing ten for ten dirhams, and the silver is destroyed: if its value equals its weight, the debt is discharged by consensus. If its value is less than its weight (e.g. value 8), or more (e.g. 12), it is the same with Abu Hanifa, because quality is not considered. With the two, the mortgagee guarantees its value from a different genus; because if only weight were considered without quality, and value was dropped, it would harm one party: the mortgagee if value is lower, the pledgor if higher. If value were considered and deemed receipt, it would lead to riba. So it is determined that he guarantees its value from a different genus. Then with Imam (Abu Hanifa): if the debt and the pledge are equal in weight, it is obvious; if the debt is more, the excess is in the pledgor's liability; if the pledge is more, the excess is a trust. If these items are pledged with a different genus, they are destroyed by their value like other property, which is clear. This is the summary of what is in al-Ayni, al-Fath etc., so memorize it. "On condition that the buyer pledge" etc. means whoever sells a slave with this condition, the sale is valid by istihsan. The qiyas is that it is not valid because it is a condition not required by the contract and contains benefit for one party, and it is a sale within a sale, which is prohibited. The istihsan argument: it is a condition suitable to the contract because surety and pledge are for security, which suits the obligation of the price. So if the pledge is specific, the meaning of the condition (security) is considered, so the contract is valid; otherwise the specific condition is considered, and the contract is invalid. (Fath) "Then if he refuses" etc. means if the sale is valid with this condition, and the buyer later refuses to give the pledge, he is not compelled. Zufar said he is compelled because by the condition it became a right of his (the seller) like a stipulated agency in a pledge contract. The response is that a pledge contract is a donation (tabarru') like giving a guarantee, and one is not compelled to donate. It only becomes a right once it exists, and it did not exist after the sale. A promise to pledge is not superior to an actual pledge; even if he actually pledges, it is not binding until he delivers, so it is even less binding by promise. (Fath) "And the seller may rescind the sale" etc. means the buyer is not compelled to pledge, but the seller has the option to rescind the sale because the condition (pledge) is a desirable attribute, and its absence gives an option. However, if the buyer pays the price immediately, the seller has no option to rescind, because the purpose is achieved; or if he gives the value of the stipulated pledge as a pledge, because the purpose of the stipulated pledge is achieved by value. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings. First, it establishes that items which are heavy (stone-like: gold, silver), measured (mikyal: eg. wheat, barley), or weighed (mawzun: eg. iron, brass) are valid for pledge because they can be valued and recovered from. Then it discusses the case where similar items are pledged: if gold is pledged for a debt of gold, and it is destroyed, the debt is discharged by weight, not value, according to Abu Hanifa. Quality is ignored. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they say the mortgagee must guarantee the value from a different genus to avoid harm. The text explains the reasoning: if only weight is considered, it may harm one party; if value, it leads to riba; so the compromise is to guarantee value from a different genus. The final part deals with a conditional pledge in a contract of sale. If a seller stipulates that the buyer gives a specific pledge for the price, the sale is valid by istihsan (even though qiyas would forbid it). However, the buyer cannot be forced to give the pledge; if he refuses, the seller may rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price immediately or gives an equivalent value as pledge. Zufar argues the buyer should be compelled, but the Hanafi response is that a pledge is a donation, not compulsory.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus or class of items; here referring to same category (e.g., gold with gold).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a source of law overriding qiyas for equity or necessity.
شرط (shart): Condition; here a stipulation in the contract of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pledged silver bar weighing 10 ounces is destroyed when the debt is 10 silver dirhams (same genus), and the silver's market value is 12 dirhams, how is the debt discharged according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Debt discharged by value of 12 dirhams.
B) Debt discharged by weight of 10 ounces, regardless of value.
C) The mortgagee must compensate with value from a different genus.
D) The debt remains and the mortgagee owns the silver.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates pledges of weighed/measured items and conditional pledges in sale by istihsan, but the buyer is not compelled to fulfil the condition; if destruction of similar-genus items occurs, the debt is discharged by weight, though the Sahibayn's view of value from different genus is often preferred to avoid harm.

Liability When a Pawn of the Same Genus Perishes
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on pawn perishing with its own kind

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pawn of the same genus as the debt perishes and explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When a pawn of the same genus perishes, Abu Hanifa cancels debt by weight; Sahibayn require value from a different genus to avoid harm and riba.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a pawn that perishes when it is of the same genus as the debt (e.g., silver for silver). The core question is whether the creditor is considered to have received the debt by weight or by value. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to riba and fairness in commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The passage deals with a pawn that is of the same genus (jins) as the debt. Note the condition: the pawn is weighed or measured (e.g., silver, gold, food).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that when the pawn perishes, the debt is cancelled by the weight/measure of the pawn, regardless of its market value or quality.
He considers the creditor to have received (istafa) the debt by weight.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn argue that the pledgee must guarantee the value of the pawn from a different genus (khilaf al-jins), turning the pawn into a guarantee and the pledgee owns the perished item by virtue of compensation.
They fear harm (darar) to either party if only weight is considered, and riba if value is directly set off.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Work through the example: pawn of 10 dirhams weight with value 8 or 12. Under Abu Hanifa, debt cancels by weight regardless. Under Sahibayn, value from different genus is guaranteed to avoid harm and potential riba.
Note that if value equals weight, all agree.
5
Apply the rule to different genera
If pawn is of a different genus (e.g., silver for gold), the dispute does not apply; it follows the general rule: perishes by value.
The commentary clarifies this at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن رهنت بجنسها هلكت من الدين، ولا عبرة بالجودة. هلكت من الدين إلخ: يعني إذا رهنت هذه الأشياء بجنسها، وهلكت عند المرتمن هلكت بمثلها من الدين وزنا أوكيلا لا قيمة، سواء كانت قيمة هذه الأشياء كوزنها أو لا، ولا عبرة بالجودة؛ لأنها ساقطة الاعتبار عند المقابلة بالجنس، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة؛ فإن عنده يصير مستوفيا باعتبار الوزن دون القيمة، وعندهما: يضمن القيمة من خلاف الجنس، فتكون رهنا مكانه ويملك المرتمن الهالك بالضمان بيانه إذا رهن الراهن فضة وزنه عشرة بعشرة دراهم وهلك الفضة فإن كانت قيمته مثل وزن عشرة، يسقط الدين بالاتفاق، وإن كانت قيمته أقل من وزنه بأن كانت قيمة الفضة ثمانية مثلا، أو كانت قيمته أكثر من عشرة بأن كانت اثنى عشرة درهما، فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم اعتبار صفة الجودة. وعندهما: يضمن المرتمن قيمته من خلاف جنسه؛ لأنه لو اعتبر الوزن وحده من غير اعتبار صفة جودة أو رداءة، وأسقط القيمة، لزم الإضرار بأحدهما يعني بالمرتمن إذا كانت أقل من وزنه، وبالراهن فيما إذا كانت القيمة أكثر، ولو اعتبر القيمة وجعل مستوفيا باعتبارها أدى إلى الربا، فتعين ما ذكر من أنه يضمن قيمته من خلاف، ثم عند الإمام: إن تساويا الدين والرهن في الوزن فظاهر وإن كان الدين أزيد فالزائد في ذمة الراهن، وإن كان الرهن أزيد فالزائد أمانة ولو رهن هذه الأشياء بخلاف جنسها، فهلكت هلكت بقيمتها كسائر الأموال وهو ظاهر، هذا حاصل ما في "العيني والفتح وغيرهما"، فاحفظه.
If you pawn with its own kind, it perishes from the debt, and quality is not considered. (The commentary says): meaning if you pawn these items with their own kind, and they perish with the pledgee, they perish by their like in weight or measure, not value, whether the value equals the weight or not, and quality is not considered because it is disregarded when matched with kind. This is according to Abu Hanifa, for he considers the receiver having received by weight, not value. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees the value from a different kind, so it becomes a pawn in its place, and the pledgee owns the perished by compensation. Explanation: If the debtor pawns silver weighing ten with ten dirhams and the silver perishes, if its value equals its weight of ten, the debt drops by agreement. If its value is less than its weight, e.g., value eight, or more, e.g., twelve, the same according to Abu Hanifa due to disregard of quality. According to the two, the pledgee guarantees its value from a different kind because if only weight were considered without quality and value dropped, harm would befall one of them—the pledgee if less, the pawner if more. If value were considered and receipt based on it, it would lead to riba. So what was mentioned—that he guarantees its value from a different kind—is determined. Then according to the Imam: if debt and pawn are equal in weight, it is obvious; if debt is more, the excess is in the pawner's liability; if pawn is more, the excess is a trust. And if one pawns these items with a different kind, they perish at their value like other wealth, which is apparent. This is the gist of what is in 'Ayni and Fath and others, so memorize it.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pawn that perishes when it is of the same genus as the debt (e.g., silver pawned for a silver debt). The matn states that the pawn cancels the debt by weight, not value, and quality is irrelevant. The commentary explains the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the creditor is considered to have received the debt by weight; thus, if the pawn perishes, the debt is discharged by its weight regardless of its market value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that this could harm one party—if the pawn's value is less than its weight, the creditor loses; if more, the debtor loses. They propose that the pledgee must compensate the pawner for the value from a different type of property, avoiding riba that would arise if value were directly considered. The commentary then details the scenarios: if pawn and debt are equal in weight, all agree the debt is discharged. If they differ, Abu Hanifa sticks to weight, while the Sahibayn require value compensation from a different genus. The passage concludes that if the pawn is of a different genus (e.g., silver for gold), it perishes at its value like any other property.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus or type of property that is weighed or measured (e.g., gold, silver, foodstuffs).
استيفاء (istifa'): Receipt or taking possession of a debt by the creditor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a pawn of the same genus as the debt perishes, how is the debt cancelled?
A) By the market value of the pawn
B) By the weight/measure of the pawn
C) By the value from a different genus
D) The debt remains entirely

Key Takeaway
When a pawn of the same genus perishes, Hanafi mufta bihi cancels the debt by weight/measure, not market value, disregarding quality to avoid riba.

Sale with Condition to Pawn: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on sale conditioned on pawning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on the buyer pawning a specific item and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
A sale with a condition to pawn is valid by istihsan despite qiyas because the condition serves the contract's purpose of securing the price.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a sale where the buyer agrees to pawn a specific item for the price. While qiyas would invalidate the condition as a prohibited 'transaction within a transaction', the Hanafi school uses istihsan to validate the sale, recognizing that the condition aligns with the contract's need for security. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling and the role of istihsan in overriding strict analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale of a slave (or any item) conditioned on the buyer pawning a specific item. The Hanafi ruling: the sale is valid (sahih) by istihsan.
2
Recognise the qiyas position
By qiyas, the sale would be invalid (fasid) because the condition is not required by the contract, benefits one party, and constitutes a prohibited 'safqah fi safqah' (transaction within a transaction).
The hadith prohibiting two transactions in one is the basis for the qiyas.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan considers the purpose (maqsad) of the condition: pawning secures the price, which suits the contract's need. Since the condition is 'suitable' (mulaim), the contract is valid. If the pawn is specified, the meaning (securing) is considered; otherwise the literal condition is considered and it would be invalid.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Example: A sells a car to B on condition that B pawns his watch. If B agrees, the sale is valid. If the condition were vague ('pawn something'), it might be invalid because the securing purpose is not achieved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن. يرهن المشتري إلخ: يعني من باع عبدا على هذا الشرط المذكور جاز البيع استحسانا، والقياس أن لا يجوز؛ لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وفيه نفع لأحد المتعاقدين، ولأنه صفقة في صفقة، وهو منهي عنه، وجه الاستحسان أنه شرط ملائم للعقد؛ لأن الكفالة والرهن للاستيثاق، وهو يلائم وجوب الثمن، فإذا كان الرهن معينا اعتبر معنى الشرط وهو الاستيثاق، فصح العقد، وإلا اعتبر عين الشرط ففسد. (فتح) فامتنع إلخ: أي إذا جاز البيع هذا الشرط، وامتنع بعد ذلك المشتري عن الرهن لا يجبر، وقال زفر: يجبر؛ لأنه بالشرط صار حقا من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في عقد الرهن وجوابه أن عقد الرهن تبرع كإعطاء الكفيل، جبر على المتبرع، وإنما يصير حقا من حقوقه إذا وجد، ولم يوجد بعد البيع والوعد بالرهن لا يكون فوق الرهن، ولو رهنه لا يلزم ما لم يسلم، فلأن لا يصير لازما بالوعد أولى. (فتح) وللبائع فسخ البيع إلخ: يعني لا يجبر المشتري على الرهن ولكن للبائع فسخ البيع؛ لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه، وفواته يوجب الخيار، إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالا، فحينئذ ليس للبائع خيار الفسخ؛ لحصول المقصود، أو يدفع قيمة الرهن المشروط رهنا؛ لأن المقصود من الرهن المشروط يحصل بالقيمة. (فتح، عيني)
Concerning 'that the buyer pawns' etc.: meaning whoever sold a slave on this mentioned condition, the sale is valid by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not valid because it is a condition not necessitated by the contract and it benefits one of the contractors, and because it is a transaction within a transaction which is prohibited. The face of istihsan is that it is a condition suitable to the contract because guarantee and pawn are for securing, and they suit the obligation of the price. So if the pawn is specified, the meaning of the condition (securing) is considered, so the contract is valid; otherwise the specific condition is considered and it is invalid. (Fath) 'So he refrains' etc.: meaning if the sale is valid with this condition, and then the buyer refrains from pawning, he is not compelled. Zufar said: he is compelled because by the condition it became a right of his like the agency stipulated in the contract of pawn. The answer is that the contract of pawn is a donation like giving a guarantor, and one is not compelled to donate. It only becomes a right when it exists, and after the sale it does not exist; a promise to pawn is not superior to actual pawn, and even if he pawns, it is not binding until delivery, so it is even less likely to be binding by promise. (Fath) 'And the seller has the option to rescind the sale' etc.: meaning the buyer is not compelled to pawn, but the seller has the option to rescind the sale because the condition is a desirable feature and its absence gives an option. Except if the buyer pays the price immediately, then the seller does not have the option to rescind because the purpose is achieved, or if he pays the value of the stipulated pawn because the purpose of the stipulated pawn is achieved by its value. (Fath, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage discusses a sale where the buyer agrees to pawn a specific item for the price. The matn states that if the buyer then refuses to pawn, he is not compelled, but the seller has the option to rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price or the value of the pawn. The commentary explains the ruling: such a sale is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) even though qiyas would invalidate it because the condition is not inherent to the contract and resembles a prohibited double transaction. The reasoning for istihsan is that the condition is compatible with the contract's purpose of securing the price. Regarding compulsion, Zufar argues the buyer can be forced because the condition becomes a right, but the Hanafi position is that pawning is a gratuitous act, so no compulsion exists. The seller's option to rescind is granted because the condition is a desired quality; if it is not fulfilled, the seller may cancel the sale. However, if the buyer pays the price immediately or pays the value of the stipulated pawn, the option ceases because the goal of security is achieved.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to suitability of the condition to the contract's purpose.
صفقة في صفقة (safqah fi safqah): A transaction within a transaction, generally prohibited in hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school validate a sale conditioned on pawning despite the hadith about two transactions?
A) Because pawning is a separate contract that is valid on its own.
B) Because the condition is suitable (mulaim) and serves the contract's purpose of security.
C) Because the hadith is considered weak by Hanafis.
D) Because the buyer has the option to rescind.

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on a specified pawn is valid by istihsan because the condition serves the contract's purpose of securing the price.
