Neither Party May Take Pledge from Trustee: Rulings and Liability
Ruling on taking pledge from trustee and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why neither the pledgor nor the pledgee may unilaterally take the pledge from the trustee, and explain the trustee's liability if he gives it to one party and the pledgee's liability if it is destroyed.

Core Idea
The trustee is a depositary for both; giving to one makes him liable, and destruction is on the pledgee.

In a valid pledge (rahn), a trustee (adl) holds the pledged item. Both the pledgor and pledgee have rights in it. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, explained by Ayni and Fath al-Qadir, clarifies two key rulings: first, neither party can take the pledge unilaterally; second, if it is destroyed, the pledgee bears the loss. Understanding these rules ensures the rights of both parties are protected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a trustee giving the pledge to one of the parties (pledgor or pledgee). The ruling is that the trustee becomes liable (daman) for the pledge.
Liability arises because the trustee is a depositary for both, and giving to one is like giving to a stranger.
2
Understand the basis: the trustee's dual role
The trustee is a depositary (mudi') for the pledgor regarding the physical object and for the pledgee regarding its financial value. Each party is a stranger to the other in this relationship.
This dual agency prevents unilateral action by either party.
3
Apply the destruction ruling
If the pledge is destroyed in the trustee's hand, it is in the guarantee of the pledgee. The trustee's hand is considered the hand of the pledgee in terms of financial value.
The guarantee is for the lesser of the pledge's value or the debt.
4
Note the guarantee amount
The pledgee's liability is capped at the lower of the pledge's market value or the outstanding debt.
This ensures the pledgee does not profit beyond the debt.
5
Synthesize the overall principle
The trustee's hand represents both parties' rights. Neither party can revoke the other's right by taking the pledge alone, and the pledgee bears the risk of destruction because he benefits from the pledge's financial value.
This balances the interests of pledgor, pledgee, and trustee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يأخذه أحدهما إلخ : أي الراهن أو المرتهن؛ لأنه تعلق به حقهما فلا يملك أحدهما إبطال الآخر، ولو دفع إلى أحدهما ضمن؛ لأنه مودع الراهن في حق العين، ومودع المرتهن في حق المالية، وكل منهما أجنبي عن الآخر، والمودع يضمن بالدفع إلى الأجنبي. (عيني، فتح) ويهلك إلخ : يعني لو هلك الرهن في يد العدل هلك في ضمان المرتمن؛ لأنه في يد المرتمن حكما؛ لأن يد العدل يد المرتمن في حق المالية، وهي مضمونة بالأقل من قيمة الرهن ومن الدين والحاصل أن العدل يده كيد كل من الراهن والمرتمن؛ لتعلق حقهما به الراهن في حفظه والمرتهن في استيفائه من ماليته؛ ولهذا لم يكن لأحدهما أخذه على الخصوص؛ لما فيه إبطال حق الآخر. (فتح)
And neither one may take it from him, etc.: meaning neither the pledgor nor the pledgee, because both have a right attached to it, so neither can revoke the other's right. If one gives it to one of them, he becomes liable, because he is a depositary for the pledgor regarding the physical object, and a depositary for the pledgee regarding the financial value, and each is a stranger to the other, and a depositary is liable when giving to a stranger. (Ayni, Fath) And it is destroyed, etc.: meaning if the pledge is destroyed in the hand of the trustee, it is destroyed in the guarantee of the pledgee, because it is in the hand of the pledgee legally, since the trustee's hand is the hand of the pledgee in terms of financial value, and it is guaranteed by the lower of the value of the pledge or the debt. The conclusion is that the trustee's hand is like the hand of both the pledgor and the pledgee, due to both their rights attaching to it: the pledgor's right in safekeeping and the pledgee's right in recovering from its value. Therefore neither may take it specifically, because that would revoke the other's right. (Fath)
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage expands on two rulings from the matn. First, neither the pledgor nor the pledgee can take the pledge from the trustee, because both have rights in it. If the trustee gives it to either, he becomes liable as a depositary giving to a stranger. Second, if the pledge is destroyed in the trustee's hand, it is in the guarantee of the pledgee, because the trustee's hand is considered the pledgee's hand regarding financial value. The guarantee covers the lesser of the pledge's value or the debt. Thus, the trustee's hand is like that of both parties, preventing unilateral taking.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability. The pledge is in the guarantee of the pledgee if destroyed.
مودع (mudi' / mustawda'): Depositary. The trustee is a depositary for each party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The trustee's dual agency means neither party can unilaterally take the pledge, and destruction falls on the pledgee.

Agency for Sale of a Pledge: Validity and Conditional Agency
Rulings on appointing an agent to sell the pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of agency for selling a pledge at maturity, explain why it can be conditional, and identify the disputed issue regarding agency of a minor.

Core Idea
Agency to sell a pledge is valid even if conditional, because it is a relinquishment of the owner's right.

The pledgor may appoint an agent to sell the pledged item when the debt matures. This agency can be made conditional on a future event, such as the maturity date. In this lesson, we examine the general ruling, the principle that allows conditional agency, and an intra-madhhab dispute about appointing a minor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is appointing an agent to sell the pledge at maturity. According to the Hanafi school, this is valid (sahih). Confirm this from the source text: 'فإن وكل ... صح'.
The agent can be the pledgee, trustee, or any other eligible person.
2
Analyze the basis for conditional agency
The text states that agency may be made conditional because it is a form of isqat (relinquishment). Understand this: the owner's right to withhold permission is relinquished by authorization. Relinquishment can be suspended. Trace the reasoning: 'لأن الوكالة تجوز تعليقها بالشرط؛ لكونها من الإسقاطات'.
This is a key usul principle applied in muamalat.
3
Examine the minor agency dispute
If the pledgor appoints a minor as agent, and the minor sells after reaching majority, Abu Hanifa says it is invalid; the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid because the agent had ability at the time of compliance. Identify the thamarah: if the sale occurs after majority, the two disciples consider it valid, while Abu Hanifa does not.
The mufta bihi position is the view of the two disciples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن وكل المرتهن أو العدل أو غيرهما ببيعه عند حلول الدين صح، صح: أي صح هذا التوكيل؛ لأن الراهن مالك، فله أن يوكل من الأهل ببيع . ماله معلقا ومنجزا؛ لأن الوكالة تجوز تعليقها بالشرط؛ لكونها من الإسقاطات؛ لأن المانع من التصرف حق المالك، وبالتسليط على بيعه أسقط حقه، والإسقاطات يجوز تعليقها بالشروط. ولو وكل صغيرا فباعه بعد بلوغه لا يصح عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن أمره وقع باطلا؛ لعدم القدرة وقت الأمر، فلا ينقلب جائزا، وعندهما يصح؛ لقدرته عليه وقت الامتثال. (تكملة، فتح) وإن شرطت في عقد الرهن لم ينعزل بعزله وبموت الراهن والمرتمن، وللوكيل بيعه بغيبة ورثته وتبطل بموت الوكيل ولا يبيعه المرتهن أو الراهن إلا برضاء الآخر. وإن شرطت إلخ يعني إن شرطت الوكالة في عقد الرهن بأن يقول الراهن رهنته على أن يكون فلانا وكيلا ببيع الرهن عند حلول الأجل، فليس للراهن أن يعزله، ولو عزله لم ينعزل بعزله، إلا إذا رضي المرتمن بذلك؛ لأن الوكالة لما شرطت في عقد الرهن صارت وصفا من أوصافه وحقا من حقوقه، فتلزم بلزوم أصله؛ ولأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن، وفي العزل اتواء حقه، وكذا لا ينعزل الوكيل بالعزل الحكمي كموت الموكل وهو الراهن، أو ارتداده، ولحوقه بدار الحرب؛ لأن الرهن لا يبطل بموته؛ لتقدم حق المرتهن على حق الورثة، وكموت المرتهن إلا أن يكون وكيلا وهذا عندنا وعند الشافعي: تبطل بموتهما. واعلم أن هذه الوكالة تخالف الوكالة المفردة، وهي التي لم تذكر في ضمن عقد الرهن من وجوه كما في "الزيلعي"، منها ما ذكره المصنف ومنها: أن الوكيل هنا إذا امتنع عن البيع يجبر عليه بخلاف الوكالة المفردة، ومنها: أن الولد والأرش بخلاف ذي المفردة، ومنها: إذا باع بخلاف جنس الدين كان له أن يصر الدين بخلاف المفردة ومنها: أن الرهن إذا كان عبدا وقتله عبد خطأ فدفع القاتل بالجناية كان لهذا الوكيل أن يبيعه بخلاف المفردة. (ملتقطا من الفتح) بيعه إلخ: أي للوكيل المذكور سواء كان المرتمن أو العدل أو غيرهما بيع الرهن بعد موت الراهن لغيبة الورثة كما كان حال حياته البيع بغير حضرته؛ لأنه لم ينعزل بموت الراهن. (كما مر من رد المحتار) وتبطل بموت الوكيل إلخ : يعني تبطل الوكالة بموت الوكيل مطلقا سواء كان مرتهنا أو عدلا أو غيرهما، ولا يقوم وارثه ولا وصيه مقامه؛ لأن الوكالة لا تجري فيها الوراثة؛ لأن هذا حق عليه والوراثة إنما تجري فيما له لا فيما عليه، ولأنهما رضيا برأيه لا برأي غيره، لكن الرهن باق بحاله؛ لأن الرهن لو كان في يد المرتهن فمات لم يبطل العقد به فلأن لا يبطل بموت العدل أولى، ولأن التسليط بالبيع أمر زائد فيه فلا يبطل الرهن لبطلانه، فإن أوصى العدل ببيعه لم يجز؛ لأنه لا يقدر على إقامة غيره مقام نفسه في حال الحياة، فلأن لا يملك بعد الوفاة وقد بطلت وكالته أولى إلا أن يكون الراهن قال في أصل الوكالة وكلتك ببيع الرهن وأجزت لك ما صنعت فيه من شيء فحينئذ يجوز لوصيه بيعه، ولا يجوز لوصيه أن يوصي به إلى ثالث، وعن أبي يوسف إن وصي الوكيل كمضارب مات والمال عروض، قلنا: المضارب يملك التوكيل حيا، فيقوم عنه وصيه ميتا، ولا كذلك يملك بيعه الوكيل. (كذا في الفتح ورد المحتار) ولا يبيعه المرتمن إلخ: يعني لا يملك أحدهما بيع الرهن إلا برضاء الآخر لتعلق حقهما به معا، فلا يملك أحدهما إبطال حق صاحبه بغير إذنه. (فتح بتغيير)
If the pledgee or the trustee or someone else appoints someone to sell it at maturity, it is valid. Valid: meaning this appointment is valid, because the pledgor is the owner, so he may appoint someone to sell his property conditionally or absolutely, because agency may be made conditional, as it is a form of relinquishment. The impediment to disposition is the owner's right, and by authorizing sale he has relinquished that right, and relinquishments may be made conditional. If he appointed a minor and the minor sold after reaching majority, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, because the command was void due to inability at the time of command, so it does not become valid later. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is valid because the agent had ability at the time of compliance. (Tatimma, Fath) If the agency is stipulated in the contract of pledge, it is not revoked by his dismissal, nor by the death of the pledgor or pledgee, and the agent may sell it in the absence of the heirs. And it is voided by the death of the agent, and neither the pledgee nor the pledgor may sell it except with the consent of the other. And if stipulated, etc. meaning: if the agency is stipulated in the contract of pledge—such as the pledgor saying, 'I pledge this on condition that so-and-so is the agent to sell the pledge at maturity'—then the pledgor may not dismiss him, and if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed by that dismissal, unless the pledgee consents to it; because when the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, it becomes a quality of it and a right of its rights, so it becomes binding by the binding of its origin; and because the pledgee's right is attached to it, and in dismissing him there is a violation of his right. Similarly, the agent is not dismissed by a constructive dismissal such as the death of the principal who is the pledgor, or his apostasy, or his joining the abode of war; because the pledge does not become void by his death, due to the precedence of the pledgee's right over the rights of heirs. Likewise, the death of the pledgee (unless he was the agent). This is with us (Hanafis), while al-Shafi'i says: the agency is voided by the death of both. Know that this agency differs from an independent agency (one not mentioned within the pledge contract) in several aspects as mentioned in al-Zayla'i: some of which are mentioned by the author; among them: that if the agent here refuses to sell, he is compelled to do so, unlike an independent agency; that the child and the price (?) are different; that if he sells for a different type than the debt, he has the right to...; that if the pledge is a slave and someone kills him by mistake and the killer pays blood money, this agent may sell it, unlike an independent agency. (Selected from al-Fath) His selling, etc.: meaning the aforementioned agent, whether the pledgee, trustee, or someone else, may sell the pledge after the death of the pledgor in the absence of the heirs, just as he could sell in his presence during his life, because he is not dismissed by the death of the pledgor. (As mentioned in Radd al-Muhtar) And it is voided by the death of the agent, etc.: meaning the agency is voided by the death of the agent absolutely, whether he is a pledgee, trustee, or other. His heir or executor does not take his place, because agency does not involve inheritance, since this is a right upon him, and inheritance only applies to rights that are for him, not against him. Also, both parties consented to his opinion, not the opinion of another. But the pledge remains as it is, because if the pledge were in the hand of the pledgee and he died, the contract would not be voided by his death, so the same applies even more to the trustee because the authorization of sale is an additional matter, so the pledge is not voided by the voidance of the agency. If the trustee bequeaths its sale, it is not permitted, because he cannot appoint someone else in his place during his life, so even more he cannot after death when his agency has already ended, unless the pledgor said in the original agency: 'I appoint you to sell the pledge and I permit you to do whatever you want with it.' Then his executor may sell it, but the executor may not appoint a third party. From Abu Yusuf: if the executor of the agent is like a mudarib who died while the capital was inventory, we say the mudarib may appoint an agent during his life, so his executor takes his place after death, but the same does not apply to the sale by the agent? (As in al-Fath and Radd al-Muhtar) And neither the pledgee nor the pledgor may sell it except with the consent of the other, meaning neither can sell the pledge except with the consent of the other, because both have rights attached to it together, so neither can revoke the right of the other without his permission. (Fath with modification)
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers several rulings on agency (wakala) for the sale of a pledge. The core rulings: (1) It is valid for the pledgor to appoint an agent (the pledgee, trustee, or someone else) to sell the pledge at maturity, and the agency can be made conditional. (2) If the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract itself, it becomes irrevocable: the pledgor cannot dismiss the agent, and it is not revoked by the death of the pledgor or pledgee (contra Shafi'i). The agent may even sell after the pledgor's death without the heirs' presence. (3) The agency is voided by the death of the agent, and no one steps in. (4) Neither the pledgor nor pledgee may sell the pledge without the other's consent. The passage also highlights differences between this 'embedded agency' and a separate agency: the agent can be compelled to sell, can sell for a different type of debt, etc. There is also an intra-Hanafi dispute about appointing a minor as agent.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakala): Agency: the appointment of someone to act on behalf of the principal in a legal matter.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bil-shart): Making a contract conditional upon a future event. Here, agency can be made conditional on the maturity of the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why agency can be conditional in Hanafi law?
A) Because it is a contract of exchange
B) Because it is a form of isqat (relinquishment)
C) Because it is a gift
D) Because it is a sale

Key Takeaway
Agency to sell a pledge can be made conditional because it involves relinquishment of the owner's right, and is valid even if the agent is a minor who later attains majority according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Embedded Agency in Pledge Contracts: Irrevocability and Survival of Death
Rulings on agency stipulated in the pledge contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an agency stipulated in a pledge contract is irrevocable and survives the death of the pledgor/pledgee, and contrast this with ordinary agency and the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When agency is embedded in a pledge contract, it becomes part of the binding contract and cannot be revoked or voided by death.

If the agency to sell the pledged item is written as a condition in the pledge contract itself, it gains special strength. The agent cannot be dismissed, and the agency continues even after the death of the pledgor or pledgee. This lesson explores these rules and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the embedded agency
The text describes when the agency is 'stipulated in the contract of pledge' (شرطت في عقد الرهن). This means the agency is a condition of the pledge contract itself, not a separate contract. Identify the effects: irrevocability and survival of death.
This is different from a separate agency contract.
2
Analyze the effect: irrevocability
The pledgor cannot dismiss the agent; if he tries, it is ineffective. The reason: the agency becomes a 'quality' of the pledge contract and the pledgee's right is attached.
The text: 'فليس للراهن أن يعزله'.
3
Analyze the effect: survival of death
The agency is not voided by the death of the pledgor or the pledgee. The reason: the pledgee's right precedes the rights of heirs. The agent can sell even in the absence of heirs.
Contrast with ordinary agency which ends with death.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that the agency is voided by death of either party. State the thamarah: under Hanafi, the sale is valid; under Shafi'i, a new agency is needed.
This is a major difference that affects practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ملتقطا من الفتح) بيعه إلخ: أي للوكيل المذكور سواء كان المرتمن أو العدل أو غيرهما بيع الرهن بعد موت الراهن لغيبة الورثة كما كان حال حياته البيع بغير حضرته؛ لأنه لم ينعزل بموت الراهن. Commentary
This lengthy passage covers several rulings on agency (wakala) for the sale of a pledge. Compelling the Agent to Sell the Pledge: Analogy to Litigation Agent
Ruling with analogy: agent compelled to sell pledge like agent for litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an agent for selling a pledge is compelled to sell when the pledgor is absent, and explain the analogy to a litigation agent.

Core Idea
An agent's refusal to sell the pledge when the pledgor is absent threatens the mortgagee's right, so the judge compels him—just as a litigation agent is compelled.

In a mortgage (rahn), the pledged property is held by a trusted person (adl). If the pledgor disappears at the debt's maturity and the agent refuses to sell, the mortgagee's right to repayment is at risk. The Hanafi school solves this by compelling the agent to sell, drawing on the established rule for agents in litigation. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the method of compulsion, and its legal basis through clear analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
Determine who is the pledge holder (adl/agent), the mortgagee (murtahin), and the pledgor (rahn). Understand the agent's duty to sell at maturity.
The adl is a custodian with authority to sell if stipulated or by court order.
2
State the ruling and its conditions
The agent is compelled to sell when (a) the debt term has expired and (b) the pledgor is absent. The compulsion applies regardless of whether the agency was stipulated in the contract.
This is the correct view (sahih) in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the method of compulsion
The judge first imprisons the agent for a few days. If he still refuses, the judge sells the pledge on his behalf. The sale is valid because it is ijbar bi haqq (compulsion by right), not ikrah (unlawful duress).
The sale is for debt repayment; the method is secondary.
4
Trace the analogy to litigation agent
Just as an agent for litigation (wakil bi al-khusuma) is compelled to appear when the principal is absent, the pledge agent is compelled. The common factor (illa) is that refusal would nullify a right that the right-holder cannot enforce directly.
In litigation, the plaintiff cannot sue a missing defendant; in pledge, the mortgagee cannot sell the pledge himself.
5
Distinguish from ordinary sale agency
In ordinary sale, the principal can sell the property himself, so no right is nullified by the agent's refusal. Therefore, no compulsion arises.
This distinction highlights the illa: inability of the right-holder to act directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرهن يوضع على يد عدل فإن حل الأجل وغاب الراهن أجبر الوكيل على بيعه كالوكيل بالخصومة إذا وكله أجبر عليها.
فإن حل الأجل إلخ: يعني إن حل الأجل الذي وكله ببيع الرهن عنده، وأبي الوكيل الذي في يده الرهن أن يبيعه وقد غاب الراهن، أجبر الوكيل على بيعه مطلقا، سواء كانت الوكالة مشروطة في العقد أولا على الصحيح؛ لأنه تعلق به حق المرتمن وفي الامتناع إبطال حقه فيجبر عليه ولأن الوكالة بالشرط في العقد صارت أوصاف الرهن فلزمت كلزومه، وكيفية الإجبار أن يحبسه القاضي أياما ليبيع، فإن امتنع بعد الحبس، فالقاضي يبيع عليه، ولا يفسد البيع بهذا الإجبار؛ لأنه وقع على قضاء الدين بأي طريق شاء حتى لو قضاه بغيره صح، وإنما البيع طريق من طرقه؛ ولأنه إجبار بحق، ومثله لا يكون مكرها. (تكملة، فتح، عيني) كالوكيل بالخصومة إلخ أي كما يجبر الوكيل بالخصومة عليها إذا غاب موكله وأبى هو عن الخصومة أجبر عليها أي على الخصومة والجامع بينهما إبطال الحق في الامتناع بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع؛ لأن الموكل يبيع بنفسه، فلا يبطل حقه أما المدعي فلا يقدر على الدعوى على الغائب والمرتمن لا يملك البيع بنفسه. [رمز الحقائق: ٤١٢/٢]
The pledge is placed with a trustworthy person. When the term expires and the pledgor is absent, the agent is compelled to sell it, like the agent for litigation when he is authorized, he is compelled to it. 'When the term expires etc.' means: when the term for which he was authorized to sell the pledge arrives, and the agent who has the pledge refuses to sell it while the pledgor is absent, the agent is compelled to sell it absolutely, whether the agency was stipulated in the contract or not, according to the correct view; because the mortgagee's right is attached to it, and refusal nullifies his right, so he is compelled. And because the agency by stipulation in the contract becomes an attribute of the pledge, so it becomes binding like the pledge itself. The method of compulsion is that the judge imprisons him for days to sell; if he still refuses after imprisonment, the judge sells on his behalf. The sale is not invalidated by this compulsion because it is for repaying the debt by any means; even if he repays otherwise, it is valid. Selling is just one method. And because it is compulsion by right, such compulsion does not render the sale invalid (as under duress). (Takmila, Fath, Ayni) 'Like the agent for litigation etc.' means: just as the agent for litigation is compelled to litigate when his principal is absent and he himself refuses, he is compelled to it. The common factor between them is the nullification of right in refusal, unlike an agent for sale (in ordinary agency) because the principal can sell himself, so his right is not nullified. But the plaintiff cannot sue a missing defendant, and the mortgagee cannot sell by himself.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the compulsion of an agent to sell the pledged property when the pledgor (rahn) is absent at the maturity of the debt. The text begins by stating the general rule: the pledge is placed with a trustworthy person (adl). When the term expires and the pledgor is absent, the agent is compelled to sell it. The commentator then expands on this, explaining that 'when the term expires' means the term for which the agent was authorized to sell. If the agent refuses despite the pledgor's absence, the judge compels him to sell. This compulsion is absolute, whether the agency was stipulated in the mortgage contract or not, according to the correct view (al-sahih). The reason is that the mortgagee's right is attached to the pledge, and refusal would nullify that right. Additionally, the agency clause becomes an attribute of the pledge itself, binding like the pledge. The method of compulsion is imprisonment by the judge for a few days; if the agent still refuses, the judge sells on his behalf. The sale is valid because it is for repaying the debt—the judge's compulsion is lawful and does not render the sale invalid. The commentator then draws an analogy with an agent for litigation (wakil bi al-khusuma): if the principal is absent and the agent refuses to litigate, he is compelled to do so. The common factor is that refusal would nullify the right of the principal (in litigation) or the mortgagee (in pledge). This distinguishes it from an ordinary agent for sale, where the principal can sell himself, so no right is nullified. The mortgagee cannot sell the pledge himself, so the agent must be compelled.

Key Terms
عدل (adl): A trustworthy person appointed to hold the pledged property (marhun) as a neutral custodian
إجبار (ijbar): Legal compulsion by the judge to perform an act, such as selling the pledge
وكيل بالخصومة (wakil bi al-khusuma): An agent appointed to litigate on behalf of a principal in court

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the common factor (jami') between the agent for selling the pledge and the agent for litigation that justifies compulsion?
A) Both are paid agents
B) The principal is absent and refusal would nullify a right
C) Both are appointed by a judge
D) The pledged property is movable

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a pledge agent refuses to sell at maturity and the pledgor is absent, the judge compels the agent to sell by analogy to the litigation agent, because refusal would nullify the mortgagee's right.

Options of the Adl When a Sold Pledge Is Reclaimed
Ruling on the adl's options when a sold pledge is reclaimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to the adl (trustee) when a sold pledge is reclaimed by a third party, and explain the legal basis for each option.

Core Idea
When a pledge is reclaimed, the adl can seek compensation from either the pledgor or the mortgagee.

In this lesson, we explore the detailed rules that govern the situation when a mortgagee has been paid from the sale of a pledge, but the pledge is later reclaimed by its true owner. The adl, who acted as seller, is initially liable to the claimant, but then has a choice of recourse. Understanding this complex web of rights and liabilities is essential for correctly managing pledges in Islamic finance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
List the adl, pledgor, mortgagee, buyer, and claimant. The adl is the trustee who sold the pledge. The claimant is the true owner.
2
Determine the state of the pledge
Is the pledge destroyed or still existing? The rules differ for each case.
3
Trace the claimant's option
The claimant can hold the pledgor (as usurper) or the adl (as wrongful seller) liable. If he holds the pledgor, the sale is valid; if the adl, the adl must pay.
4
Analyze the adl's subsequent option
After paying the claimant, the adl can seek recourse from the pledgor for the value (as his agent) or from the mortgagee for the price (as paid without right).
5
Apply to the extant case
If the pledge is still with the buyer, the buyer recovers the price from the adl, and then the adl has similar options. Note the effect on the mortgagee's possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن باعه إلخ : يعني إن باع العدل الرهن وأوفى مرتهنه ثمنه، ثم جاء أحد يستحق الرهن، وضمن العدل للمستحق، فالعدل مخير إن شاء يضمن الراهن قيمته وإن شاء يضمن المرتمن ثمنه، وتوضيح هذا أن المرهون المبيع إذا استحق إما أن يكون هالكا أو قائما، ففي الأول المستحق بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن؛ لأنه غاصب في حقه، وإن شاء ضمن العدل؛ لأنه متعد بالبيع والتسليم، فإن ضمن الراهن نفذ البيع وصح الاقتضاء. من يده؛ لأنه وجد عين وإن ضمن العدل فكذلك، ثم هو بالخيار إن شاء رجع على الراهن بالقيمة؛ لأنه وكيل من جهته، وإن شاء رجع على المرتهن بثمنه؛ لأنه تبين أن الثمن أخذه بغير حق؛ لأنه إنما أداه إليه على حسبان أن البيع ملك الراهن، فإذا تبين أنه ليس ملكه لم يكن راضيا به فله أن يرجع به عليه، وإذا رجع بطل له الاقتضاء، فيرجع المرتمن على الراهن بدينه، وفي الثاني وهو ما إذا كان قائما في يد المشتري، فللمستحق أن يأخذه ماله، ثم للمشتري أن يرجع على العدل بالثمن؛ لأن حقوق العقد ترجع إليه، ثم هو إن شاء يرجع على الراهن بالقيمة؛ لأنه هو الذي أدخله في هذه العهدة، فإذا رجع عليه صح قبض المرتهن، وسلم له المقبوض، وبرئ الراهن عن الدين وإن شاء يرجع على المرتمن؛ لأن البيع انتقض بالاستحقاق، فبطل الثمن وقد قبضه ثمنا، فيجب عليه رده، فإذا دفعه إلى العدل عاد حقه في الدين على الراهن كما كان فيرجع به عليه.
قيمته مات بالدين، وإن ضمّن المرتمن رجع على الراهن بالقيمة وبدينه. أي العبد المستحق أي المرقمن أيضاً قيمته أي قيمة العبد المستحق الهالك مات بالدين إلخ يعني إن مات العبد المرهون عند المرتمن ثم جاءه أحد يستحقه فالمستحق بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن، وإن شاء ضمن المرتمن؛ لأن كلا منهما متعد في حقه فإذا كان كذلك، وضمن الراهن قيمته أي قيمة العبد المستحق الهالك مات العبد بالدين يعني يصبر المرتمن مستوفيا لدينه بهلاك الرهن عنده؛ لأن الراهن ملكه بأداء الضمان مستندا إلى ما قبل التسليم، فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه، ثم صار المرتمن مستوفيا بهلاك [رمز الحقائق: ٤١٣/٢] وإن ضمن المرتهن إلخ : أي وإن ضمن المرتمن رجع المرتمن على الراهن بالقيمة أي بما ضمن من قيمة العبد رجع وبدينه أيضا على الراهن، أما القيمة؛ فلأنه مغرور من جهة الراهن، وأما الدين؛ فلأنه انتقض اقتضاؤه، فيعود حقه كما كان رمز الحقائق: ٤١٣/٢]
'And if he sells it etc.' means: if the adl sold the pledge and paid its price to the mortgagee, then someone comes claiming ownership (istihqaq) of the pledge, and the adl is made liable to the claimant, then the adl has the option: if he wishes, he makes the pledgor liable for its value, or if he wishes, he makes the mortgagee liable for its price. The explanation is that if the sold pledge is reclaimed, it is either destroyed or still extant. In the first case, the claimant has the option: if he wishes, he makes the pledgor liable because he is a usurper (ghasib) in respect to his right; or if he wishes, he makes the adl liable because the adl acted wrongfully (muta'addi) by selling and delivering. If he makes the pledgor liable, the sale is valid and the recovery of the debt is valid from his hand because he found the object (ayn) [i.e., he gets value]. And if he makes the adl liable, likewise. Then the adl has the option: if he wishes, he recovers the value from the pledgor because he is his agent; or if he wishes, he recovers the price from the mortgagee because it becomes clear that the mortgagee took the price without right, since the adl paid it thinking the sale was the pledgor's property, but when it is shown not to be his, the adl was not satisfied, so he can recover it from the mortgagee. If he recovers, the mortgagee's recovery of the debt is void, and the mortgagee goes back to the pledgor for his debt. In the second case, when the pledge is still in the buyer's hand, the claimant takes his property, then the buyer recovers the price from the adl because contractual rights revert to him. Then the adl, if he wishes, recovers the value from the pledgor because he brought him into this guarantee; if he recovers from him, the mortgagee's possession is valid, the received property is confirmed, and the pledgor is free of the debt. Or if he wishes, he recovers from the mortgagee because the sale is voided by the claim, so the price is void, and the mortgagee had taken it as price, so he must return it. If he pays it to the adl, the mortgagee's right in the debt returns to the pledgor as before, and he recovers it from him. 'Its value dies with the debt, and if he makes the mortgagee liable, he recovers from the pledgor the value and his debt.' That is, if the pledged slave dies while with the mortgagee, then someone claims him, the claimant has the option to make either the pledgor or the mortgagee liable. If he makes the pledgor liable for its value (the value of the claimed slave that died), 'dies with the debt' means the mortgagee becomes satisfied for his debt by the destruction of the pledge with him, because the pledgor owns it by paying the indemnity based on a preceding delivery, so it becomes clear that he pledged his own property, then the mortgagee becomes satisfied by its destruction. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 413/2] 'And if he makes the mortgagee liable etc.' means: if the claimant makes the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee recovers from the pledgor the value (i.e., the amount he was made liable for as value of the slave) and also his debt from the pledgor. As for the value, because he was deceived (maghrur) by the pledgor; as for the debt, because his recovery is voided, so his right returns as before. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 413/2]
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the consequences when a sold pledge is reclaimed (mustahaqq) by a third party, or when the pledge dies while in the mortgagee's possession. The text first considers the scenario where the adl (trustee) sold the pledge, paid the mortgagee, and then a claimant (mustahaqq) appears. The adl is made liable to the claimant (i.e., he must compensate him). Then the adl has an option: he can seek indemnity from the pledgor (rahn) for the value (qimah) of the pledge, or from the mortgagee (murtahin) for the price (thaman) he paid. The explanation differentiates between whether the pledge is destroyed (halik) or extant (qa'im). If destroyed, the claimant can choose to hold the pledgor liable (as usurper) or the adl (as wrongful seller). If he holds the pledgor, the sale is valid and the mortgagee keeps the debt satisfied. If he holds the adl, the adl then can seek recourse from either the pledgor (as his agent) or the mortgagee (since the mortgagee received the price without right, because the adl paid it thinking the sale was valid). If the adl recovers from the mortgagee, the mortgagee's debt is revived against the pledgor. If the pledge is still in the buyer's hand, the claimant takes it, the buyer recovers the price from the adl, and then the adl has the same options: he can recover the value from the pledgor (which validates the mortgagee's possession and frees the pledgor of debt) or from the mortgagee (which revives the debt). The second main scenario: if the pledged property (e.g., a slave) dies while with the mortgagee, and then a claimant appears, the claimant has the option to hold either the pledgor or the mortgagee liable. If he holds the pledgor, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his debt because the pledge died in his possession; the pledgor, by paying the value, retroactively owns the property, so it was his own pledge, and its destruction satisfies the mortgagee. If he holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee pays the value to the claimant and then can recover that value plus his original debt from the pledgor, because he was deceived by the pledgor and his previous debt recovery is voided. This is a complex area of Hanafi law involving multiple parties and options, all based on the principle of protecting rights while ensuring the claimant is compensated.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A third party's successful claim of ownership over the pledged property, invalidating the sale
مخير (mukhayyar): Having an option or choice between two courses of action, as the adl has between seeking indemnity from pledgor or mortgagee
عدل (adl): The trusted person who acts as seller of the pledge; often translated as trustee

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the sold pledge is reclaimed and destroyed, and the claimant chooses to hold the adl liable, what is the adl's first recourse?
A) He must always recover from the pledgor
B) He can choose to recover from either the pledgor or the mortgagee
C) He must recover from the mortgagee first
D) He cannot recover from anyone

Key Takeaway
The adl's right of recourse is conditional on his having been made liable, and he may choose either the pledgor or the mortgagee depending on the case.

Liability When the Pledge Dies Before Reclamation
Ruling on liability when the pledge dies and is then claimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the options available to the claimant and the mortgagee when a pledged property dies before being claimed, and state the effect on the mortgagee's debt.

Core Idea
If a pledge dies, the claimant can hold either the pledgor or the mortgagee liable; the mortgagee may then recover from the pledgor.

This lesson deals with the situation where the pledged property perishes while in the mortgagee's possession, and then a third party comes forward to claim ownership. The rules determine who bears the loss and how the various parties can seek compensation. It is a classic Hanafi analysis of liability in pledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event
The pledge dies (halak) while with the mortgagee. Then a claimant appears claiming ownership.
2
State the claimant's option
The claimant can choose to hold the pledgor liable (as usurper) or the mortgagee liable (as bailee who is now liable because the property is claimed).
3
Apply the option if held against pledgor
If the claimant holds the pledgor liable, the pledgor pays the value. This retroactively makes him the owner, so the mortgagee's debt is considered satisfied by the pledge's destruction ('dies with the debt').
4
Apply the option if held against mortgagee
If the claimant holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee pays the value to the claimant. Then the mortgagee can recover that value plus his original debt from the pledgor, because he was deceived (maghrur) by the pledgor.
5
Note the legal reasoning
The mortgagee's recovery of his debt is voided when he pays the claimant, so his right to the debt returns to the original state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he makes the pledgor liable for its value (the value of the claimed slave that died), 'dies with the debt' means the mortgagee becomes satisfied for his debt by the destruction of the pledge with him, because the pledgor owns it by paying the indemnity based on a preceding delivery, so it becomes clear that he pledged his own property, then the mortgagee becomes satisfied by its destruction. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 413/2] 'And if he makes the mortgagee liable etc.' means: if the claimant makes the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee recovers from the pledgor the value (i.e., the amount he was made liable for as value of the slave) and also his debt from the pledgor. As for the value, because he was deceived (maghrur) by the pledgor; as for the debt, because his recovery is voided, so his right returns as before. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 413/2]
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the consequences when a sold pledge is reclaimed (mustahaqq) by a third party, or when the pledge dies while in the mortgagee's possession. The text first considers the scenario where the adl (trustee) sold the pledge, paid the mortgagee, and then a claimant (mustahaqq) appears. The adl is made liable to the claimant (i.e., he must compensate him). Then the adl has an option: he can seek indemnity from the pledgor (rahn) for the value (qimah) of the pledge, or from the mortgagee (murtahin) for the price (thaman) he paid. The explanation differentiates between whether the pledge is destroyed (halik) or extant (qa'im). If destroyed, the claimant can choose to hold the pledgor liable (as usurper) or the adl (as wrongful seller). If he holds the pledgor, the sale is valid and the mortgagee keeps the debt satisfied. If he holds the adl, the adl then can seek recourse from either the pledgor (as his agent) or the mortgagee (since the mortgagee received the price without right, because the adl paid it thinking the sale was valid). If the adl recovers from the mortgagee, the mortgagee's debt is revived against the pledgor. If the pledge is still in the buyer's hand, the claimant takes it, the buyer recovers the price from the adl, and then the adl has the same options: he can recover the value from the pledgor (which validates the mortgagee's possession and frees the pledgor of debt) or from the mortgagee (which revives the debt). The second main scenario: if the pledged property (e.g., a slave) dies while with the mortgagee, and then a claimant appears, the claimant has the option to hold either the pledgor or the mortgagee liable. If he holds the pledgor, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his debt because the pledge died in his possession; the pledgor, by paying the value, retroactively owns the property, so it was his own pledge, and its destruction satisfies the mortgagee. If he holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee pays the value to the claimant and then can recover that value plus his original debt from the pledgor, because he was deceived by the pledgor and his previous debt recovery is voided. This is a complex area of Hanafi law involving multiple parties and options, all based on the principle of protecting rights while ensuring the claimant is compensated.

Key Terms
هلاك (halak): Destruction or death of the pledged property
مغرور (maghrur): Deceived; the mortgagee is considered deceived by the pledgor when the pledge is not his property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a claimed pledge dies, and the claimant holds the mortgagee liable, what can the mortgagee then recover from the pledgor?
A) Only the value of the pledge
B) Only the original debt
C) Both the value of the pledge and the original debt
D) Nothing, because the pledge is dead

Key Takeaway
The death of the pledge does not automatically extinguish the debt; it depends on whom the claimant holds liable.

Claimant's Option When Pawned Slave Dies and Is Claimed
Ruling on pawned slave death and third-party claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pawned slave dies and a third party claims ownership, and explain why the claimant may choose to hold either the pledgor or the pledgee liable.

Core Idea
When a pawned slave dies and its true owner appears, the claimant can sue either the pledgor or the pledgee—each is a wrongdoer—and if the pledgee pays, he recovers from the pledgor.

In this passage, we examine a scenario where a pawned slave dies while in the pledgee's possession, and a third party emerges claiming rightful ownership. The Hanafi school grants this claimant a choice: he may pursue compensation from either the pledgor (the original pawner) or the pledgee (the creditor holding the pawn). This ruling flows from the principle that both parties have wronged the claimant—the pledgor by pawning what was not his, the pledgee by holding and causing the death of someone else's property. The legal consequences differ depending on whom the claimant sues, and we will trace the full chain of liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the triggering event
The pawned slave (marhun) has died in the possession of the pledgee (murtahin). A third party (mustahiq) comes forward claiming rightful ownership of that slave.
The slave is considered perished (halik).
2
State the claimant's two options
The claimant (mustahiq) has the option (al-khiyar): he may either hold the pledgor (rahin) liable for the slave's value, or hold the pledgee (murtahin) liable for the value.
The text explicitly says 'fa al-mustahiq bi al-khiyar'.
3
Understand the rationale for both being liable
Both the pledgor and the pledgee are considered muta'addi (wrongdoer/transgressor) relative to the claimant's right. The pledgor pawned property that did not belong to him; the pledgee took possession of and caused the death of property that was not his.
This is the core legal reasoning (ta'lil).
4
Trace the consequences if claimant sues the pledgor
If the pledgor pays the value, the pledgee is considered to have been fully satisfied of his debt by the destruction of the pawn. This is because the pledgor's payment retroactively confirms that the slave was his own property, so it was his own that perished.
The text says 'fa tabayyana annahu rahana malaka nafsihi'.
5
Trace the consequences if claimant sues the pledgee
If the pledgee pays the value, he can then recover from the pledgor both the value he paid (since he was deceived by the pledgor) and his original debt (since its satisfaction is now voided).
The pledgee's right to recoup is based on the principle of taghrir (deception).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيمته مات بالدين، وإن ضمّن المرتمن رجع على الراهن بالقيمة وبدينه. أي العبد المستحق أي المرقمن أيضا قيمته أي قيمة العبد المستحق الهالك مات بالدين إلخ يعني إن مات العبد المرهون عند المرتمن ثم جاءه أحد يستحقه فالمستحق بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن، وإن شاء ضمن المرتمن؛ لأن كلا منهما متعد في حقه فإذا كان كذلك، وضمن الراهن قيمته أي قيمة العبد المستحق الهالك مات العبد بالدين يعني يصبر المرتمن مستوفيا لدينه بهلاك الرهن عنده؛ لأن الراهن ملكه بأداء الضمان مستندا إلى ما قبل التسليم، فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه، ثم صار المرتمن مستوفيا بهلاك وإن ضمن المرتهن إلخ : أي وإن ضمن المرتمن رجع المرتمن على الراهن بالقيمة أي بما ضمن من قيمة العبد رجع وبدينه أيضا على الراهن، أما القيمة؛ فلأنه مغرور من جهة الراهن، وأما الدين؛ فلأنه انتقض اقتضاؤه، فيعود حقه كما كان.
His value dies with the debt, and if the pledgee guarantees, he returns upon the pledgor for the value and his debt. Meaning the claimed slave, meaning also the pledgee? Its value meaning the value of the perished claimed slave dies with the debt etc. That is, if the pawned slave dies in the possession of the pledgee, then a person comes claiming it, the claimant has the option: if he wishes, he can hold the pledgor liable, and if he wishes, he can hold the pledgee liable, because each of them is transgressing with respect to his right. When it is so, and he holds the pledgor liable for its value—meaning the value of the perished claimed slave—the slave dies with the debt, meaning the pledgee is considered satisfied for his debt by the destruction of the pawn with him, because the pledgor acquired ownership by paying the guarantee traced back to before delivery, so it becomes clear that he pawned his own property, then the pledgee becomes satisfied by destruction. And if he holds the pledgee liable, etc.: That is, if he holds the pledgee liable, the pledgee returns upon the pledgor for the value—meaning what he guaranteed of the slave's value—and also for his debt upon the pledgor. As for the value, because he is deceived by the pledgor; as for the debt, because its satisfaction is revoked, so his right returns as it was.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when a pawned slave dies in the possession of the pledgee, and a third party comes forward claiming rightful ownership of the slave. The claimant is given a choice: he may either sue the pledgor (the original owner who pawned the slave) for the slave's value, or sue the pledgee (the creditor holding the pawn). The reason both are liable is that each has wronged the claimant relative to his right: the pledgor pawned property that was not his, and the pledgee held and caused the death of property that was not his. If the claimant chooses to sue the pledgor and the pledgor pays the value, the pledgee is considered to have been fully satisfied of his debt by the destruction of the pawn, because the pledgor's payment retroactively establishes that the slave actually belonged to the pledgor, so it was his own property that perished. If instead the claimant sues the pledgee and the pledgee pays the value, the pledgee can then recover from the pledgor both the value he paid (since he was deceived by the pledgor) and his original debt (since its satisfaction is undone). This is a well-established Hanafi ruling based on the principles of guarantee and deception.

Key Terms
مستحق (mustahiq): A third party who claims rightful ownership of the pawned slave that died.
متعد (muta'addi): One who transgresses, meaning they are liable because they acted wrongfully regarding the claimant's property.
ضمان (daman): Financial liability; here it means the act of guaranteeing or paying compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the pledgor
B) Only the pledgee
C) Either the pledgor or the pledgee at his option
D) Only the one who caused the death

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a pawned object is destroyed and a true owner appears, he has the right to choose whom to hold liable, and the pledgee's recourse against the pledgor is protected.

Pledgor's Sale of the Pawn: Suspended, Void, or Effective?
Ruling on the pledgor's sale of the pawn and its validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the pledgor's sale of a pawn, distinguish it from the intra-madhhab views of the 'three' and Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling to scenarios of multiple sales and the buyer's option.

Core Idea
A pledgor's sale of a pawn is suspended—becoming effective only with the pledgee's permission or debt payment.

When a person pawns his property, he transfers a right of detention to the pledgee. What happens if he then sells the pawned item without the pledgee's consent? The Hanafi school offers a nuanced answer: the sale is not void but suspended, preserving both the pledgor's ownership and the pledgee's security. This lesson unpacks the intra-madhhab debate and its practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه توقف بيع الراهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه ونفذ عتقه وطولب بدينه ثم إن باعه الراهن بيعا ثانيا من غيره قبل إجازة المرتهن فالثاني أيضا موقوف فإن الأول موقوف والموقوف لا يمنع توقف الثاني فأيهما أجاز نفذ وبطل الآخر وكون الأول موقوفا مقيد بما إذا باعه ثانيا من أجنبي فلو باعه من المرتمن انفسخ الأول فإن أجازه المرتمن نفذ وينتقل حقه إلى البدل وإلا ينفسخ البيع في ظاهر الرواية وعند الثلاثة يبطل البيع وعن أبي يوسف أنه ينفذ لأنه تصرف في ملكه فصار كالإعتاق والصحيح ظاهر الرواية لأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن فلا ينفذ إلا بإجازته أو لقضاء الدين لزوال المانع ثم الشيخ يحيه سكت عن حكم الفسخ إذا لم يجزه المرتمن إشارة إلى أنه لا ينفسخ بفسخه وقيل له أن يجز وله أن يفسخ والصحيح أنه لا ينفسخ بفسخه لأن الامتناع لحقه كيلا يتضرر والتوقف لا يضره لأن حقه في الحبس لا يبطل الانعقاد من غير نفوذ فبقي متوقفا ثم المشتري بالخيار إن شاء صبر حتى يفك الراهن الرهن وإن شاء دفع الأمر إلى القاضي فيفسخه لأن ولاية الفسخ للقاضي لا للمشتري والبائع وهو الراهن.
Chapter on Disposal of the Pawn and Injury upon It. The sale of the pledgor is suspended upon the permission of his pledgee or the payment of his debt, and his manumission is effective, and he is asked for his debt. Then, if the pledgor sells it a second time to another before the pledgee's permission, the second is also suspended, because the first is suspended, and a suspended (transaction) does not prevent the suspension of the second. Whichever of them is permitted, it becomes effective and the other is void. And the first being suspended is restricted to when he sells it a second time to a stranger; if he sells it to the pledgee, the first is dissolved. If the pledgee permits it, it becomes effective and his right transfers to the substitute; otherwise, the sale is annulled in the apparent narration. According to the three, the sale is void. According to Abu Yusuf, it is effective, because it is a disposal of his property, so it is like manumission. The correct is the apparent narration, because the right of the pledgee is attached to it, so it is not effective except with his permission or for payment of the debt, due to removal of the obstacle. Then Sheikh Yahya? remained silent about the ruling of annulment if the pledgee does not permit it, indicating that it is not annulled by his annulment. It is said that he may permit and he may annul, but the correct is that it is not annulled by his annulment, because the abstention is for his right so that he is not harmed, and suspension does not harm him, because his right of detention does not nullify the contract without effect, so it remains suspended. Then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he waits until the pledgor redeems the pawn; if he wishes, he refers the matter to the judge, and he annuls it, because the authority of annulment belongs to the judge, not to the buyer or the seller who is the pledgor.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage deals with the pledgor's sale of the pawned property. The Hanafi ruling is that such a sale is suspended (muwaqqaf) on the pledgee's permission or the pledgor's payment of the debt. If the pledgee permits the sale, the sale becomes effective and the pledgee's right transfers to the price (substitute). If the pledgee does not permit, the sale is annulled (yunsakh) in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), which is the position of Abu Hanifa. There is, however, an intra-madhhab dispute: the 'three' (likely Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar) say the sale is batil (void ab initio) rather than having the potential to be ratified. A narration from Abu Yusuf says the sale is effective without permission, analogizing it to manumission. The relied-upon position is the apparent narration, because the pledgee has a right attached to the property, so the sale cannot be effective without his permission or elimination of the impediment. The passage also discusses a second sale: if the pledgor sells the same pawn to another buyer before the pledgee permits the first sale, the second sale is also suspended; whichever is permitted first becomes effective. If the pledgor sells to the pledgee himself, the first sale is dissolved. The buyer does not have the power to annul the sale; he can either wait until the pledgor redeems or take the matter to the judge for annulment.

Key Terms
موقوف (muwaqqaf): A legal act (sale) that is valid but its effect is suspended pending a condition or permission.
إجازة (ijazah): Permission or subsequent consent of the pledgee that makes the suspended sale effective.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or rescission of the contract, here by the judge or by the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), what is the status of a pledgor's sale of the pawn without the pledgee's permission?
A) The sale is void (batil)
B) The sale is immediately effective
C) The sale is suspended (muwaqqaf) on permission
D) The sale is voidable at the buyer's option

Key Takeaway
The pledged property is not free from the pledgee's right; thus, the pledgor's sale is suspended, not void or immediately effective, and can be ratified by the pledgee.

Manumission of Pawned Slave by Pledgor: The Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on the pledgor's manumission of the pawned slave and its immediate effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on manumission of a pawned slave, explain the Hanafi–Shafi'i disagreement, and determine the practical consequences for the pledgee's right.

Core Idea
Manumission of a pawned slave is effective immediately because ownership of the corpus outweighs the pledgee's right of detention.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi ruling that seems to override contractual rights. The key is understanding that manumission (itq) is an act of worship, and ownership of the corpus (raqaba) is stronger than the pledgee's temporary right to hold the slave. While the Hanafi school holds manumission valid even without the pledgee's consent, Imam al-Shafi'i restricts this to solvent pledgors only. Let's walk through the reasoning and its financial implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its scope
Locate the statement in the passage that manumission is effective 'absolutely, whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent.' Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
The phrase 'mutlaqan' indicates no condition.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Find the Shafi'i view: manumission is effective only if the pledgor is solvent; otherwise it is like a sale that annuls the pledgee's right.
Shafi'i bases his view on solvency being a condition.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Identify the analogy: insolvent manumission is like sale—both annul the pledgee's right. The passage says 'fa-ashbaha al-bay'a' (so it resembles sale).
Sale of a pawned item without permission is not effective.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response distinguishes manumission from sale: sale requires delivery, which is blocked by the pawn, but manumission does not. Ownership of the corpus is unaffected by the pawn, and the pledgee's right is merely possessory.
The passage gives analogies: purchased slave before delivery, escaped slave, usurped slave.
5
Apply the financial consequences
Read the latter part of the passage: after manumission, if the debt is due, the pledgor is asked to pay; if deferred, he pays the slave's value which is held as new pawn.
This shows the pledgee's right is not destroyed but transferred to compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفذ عتقه أي نفذ عتق الراهن العبد المرهون بلا إجازة المرتهن مطلقا سواء كان موسرا أو معسرا وقال الشافعي لا ينفذ إن كان معسرا وإن كان موسرا ينفذ وهو أظهر أقواله لأن في تنفيذه مع الإعسار إبطال حق المرتهن فأشبه البيع بخلاف ما إذا كان موسرا لأنه لا يبطل حقه معنى بالتضمين ولنا أنه مخاطب أعتق ملك نفسه فلا يلغو تصرفه لعدم إذن المرتهن كما إذا أعتق العبد المشتري قبل القبض أو أعتق الآبق أو المغصوب ولا خفاء في ملك الرقبة لقيام المقتضي وعارض الرهن لا ينبئ عن زواله ثم إذا زال ملكه في الرقبة بإعتاقه يزول ملك المرتمن في اليد بناء عليه كإعتاق العبد المشترك بل أولى لأن ملك الرقبة أقوى من ملك اليد وامتناع النفاذ في البيع والهبة لانعدام القدرة على التسليم وطولب إلخ يعني إذا كان الراهن موسرا والدين حالا طولب بأداء الدين لأنه لو طولب بأداء القيمة تقع بقدر الدين فلا فائدة فيه ولو مؤجلا إلخ يعني لو كان الدين مؤجلا يؤخذ من المعتق قيمة العبد وتجعل رهنا مكان العبد إذا كان موسرا لأن سبب الضمان قد تحقق وفي التضمين فائدة وهي حصول الاستيشاق من الوجه الذي بيناه ويحبسها إلى حلول الأجل فإذا حل اقتضاه بحقه إذا كان بجنسه لأن للغريم أن يستوفي حقه من مال غريمه إذا ظفر بجنس حقه وإن كان فيه فضل رده لانتهاء حكم الرهن بالاستيفاء وإن كان أقل من رجع بالزيادة لعدم ما يسقطه.
His manumission is effective: that is, the manumission by the pledgor of the pawned slave is effective without the permission of the pledgee absolutely, whether he is solvent or insolvent. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not effective if he is insolvent, but if he is solvent, it is effective, and this is the most apparent of his statements, because enforcing it with insolvency annuls the right of the pledgee, so it is analogous to the sale; unlike if he is solvent, because it does not annul his right meaning-wise due to compensation (tadmin). Our evidence is that he (the pledgor) is addressed (by the Sharia) and he manumits his own property, so his disposal is not futile due to the lack of permission of the pledgee, just as if he manumits a purchased slave before taking delivery, or manumits an escaped slave or a usurped slave. There is no concealment regarding ownership of the corpus (raqaba), due to the presence of the cause (muqtadi), and the counteracting (aarid) of pawn does not indicate its removal. Then when his ownership of the corpus ceases by his manumission, the ownership of the pledgee over the (right of) possession ceases based on it, like manumission of a jointly-owned slave—even more so, because ownership of the corpus is stronger than ownership of possession. And the prevention of effectiveness in sale and gift is due to lack of ability to deliver. And he is asked (for the debt), etc., meaning if the pledgor is solvent and the debt is due, he is asked to pay the debt, because if he were asked to pay the value, it would fall in the amount of the debt, so there is no benefit in it. And if it is deferred, etc., meaning if the debt is deferred, the value of the slave is taken from the manumitter and made a pawn in place of the slave, if he is solvent, because the cause of guarantee has been realized, and in the imposition of guarantee there is benefit, which is obtaining security in the manner we explained. He holds it (the value) until the term expires; when it expires, he collects it as his due if it is of the same type (as his debt), because a creditor may collect his due from his debtor's property if he finds a like of his right. And if there is surplus, he returns it, because the rule of pawn ends with collection; and if it is less, he gets back the deficiency, because nothing to cancel it.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on manumission ('itq) of a pawned slave by the pledgor. Unlike sale, manumission is effective immediately without the pledgee's consent, whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent. The reason is that manumission is an act of piety that the Sharia encourages, and the pledgor owns the slave's corpus (raqaba). The pawn only gives the pledgee a right of detention (haqq al-habs), which is subordinate to the ownership of the corpus. Therefore, when the pledgor manumits, the ownership of the corpus ends, and the pledgee's right of possession terminates accordingly. This is distinguished from sale and gift, which are not effective because they require delivery of possession, which is prevented by the pawn. The passage then contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i's view: he holds that if the pledgor is insolvent, the manumission is not effective because it would annul the pledgee's right entirely; but if he is solvent, it is effective because compensation can be demanded. The Hanafi response is that the ruling is based on the strength of ownership of the corpus and the fact that the pawn is only a temporary impediment that does not negate ownership. After manumission, if the debt is due, the pledgor may be asked to pay it directly. If the debt is deferred and the pledgor is solvent, he must pay the slave's value, which is held as a new pawn until the debt matures, at which point the pledgee can collect his debt from that sum.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave, which is a praiseworthy act.
موسر (musir): Solvent; having sufficient wealth to pay debts or compensation.
ملك الرقبة (milk ar-raqaba): Ownership of the corpus (of the slave), as opposed to mere possession or usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a pledgor's manumission of a pawned slave without the pledgee's permission?
A) It is not effective without permission
B) It is effective only if the pledgor is solvent
C) It is effective whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent
D) It is effective only if the debt is due

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that manumission of a pawned slave is effective immediately because ownership of the corpus trumps the pledgee's possessory right, regardless of solvency.

Suspension of the Pledgor's Sale of the Pledged Property
Ruling on suspension of pledgor's sale pending pledgee's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the pledgor's sale of pledged property without the pledgee's permission according to Zahir al-Riwayah, explain the proof, and distinguish between the Hanafi position and the views of other schools.

Core Idea
The pledgor's sale is suspended, not void — the pledgee's right must be satisfied for it to take effect.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the legal status of a sale of pledged property by the pledgor. The ruling is a classic example of the Hanafi concept of tawaqquf (suspension), where a contract is not fully effective due to an attached right of another party. The passage also presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the opposing view of the three other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being sold? By whom? What is the initial ruling according to the matn?
The act is the pledgor (debtor) selling the pledged property.
2
Identify the condition for effectiveness
Under what condition does the sale become fully effective?
Two conditions: pledgee's permission or debt repayment.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
What is the legal reasoning behind the ruling of suspension?
The proof is that the pledgee's right (haq al-irtihaan) has attached to the property.
4
Compare with other views
How do other schools and some Hanafi scholars differ?
Three schools: void; Abu Yusuf: immediately effective.
5
Understand the practical consequences
What difference does the ruling make in practice?
Thamarah al-khilaf: purchaser can wait or seek judicial rescission; void sale gives no rights; effective sale transfers right to price.

Source Text

باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه، وجنايته على غيره
الرهن
أي الراهن
توقف بيع الراهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه، ونفذ عتقه، وطولب بدينه
رهنه
لو حالا، ولو مؤجلا أخذ منه قيمة العبد، وجعلت رهنا مكانه،
لو كان الدين ولو كان الدين
الراهن
القيمة
العبد
الراهن
دين المرتمن
باب التصرف إلخ: لما كان التصرف في الرهن، والجناية عليه، وجناية على غيره متأخرا طبعا عن كونه رهنا أخره وضعا ليوافق الوضع الطبع. (تكملة) توقف بيع الراهن إلخ فإن أجازه المرتمن نفذ وينتقل حقه إلى البدل، وإلا ينفسخ البيع في ظاهر الرواية، وعند الثلاثة يبطل البيع، وعن أبي يوسف أنه ينفذ؛ لأنه تصرف في ملكه، فصار كالإعتاق، والصحيح ظاهر الرواية؛ لأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن، فلا ينفذ إلا إجازته، أو لقضاء الدين لزوال المانع، ثم الشيخ يحيه سكت عن حكم الفسخ إذا لم يجزه المرتمن إشارة إلى أنه لا ينفسخ بفسخه. وقيل: له أن يجز، وله أن يفسخ، والصحيح أنه لا ينفسخ بفسخه؛ لأن الامتناع لحقه كيلا يتضرر، والتوقف لا يضره؛ لأن حقه في الحبس لا يبطل الانعقاد من غير نفوذ، فبقي متوقفا ثم المشتري بالخيار إن شاء صبر حتى يفك الراهن الرهن، وإن شاء دفع الأمر إلى القاضي، فيفسخه؛ لأن ولاية الفسخ للقاضي لا للمشتري والبائع وهو الراهن. [رمز الحقائق: ٤١٣/٢] ثم إن باعه الراهن بيعا ثانيا من غيره قبل إجازة المرتهن، فالثاني أيضا موقوف، فإن الأول موقوف، والموقوف لا يمنع توقف الثاني، فأيهما أجاز نفذ، وبطل الآخر، وكون الأول موقوفا مقيد بما إذا باعه ثانيا من أجنبي، فلو باعه من المرتمن انفسخ الأول. (عيني، فتح، ملا مسكين)
Chapter of Disposition in the Pledge and Injury upon it, and its Injury upon others. The pledge: meaning the pledgor. The pledgor's sale is suspended upon the permission of his pledgee or the repayment of his debt, and his manumission is effective, and he is demanded for his debt. His pledge: if immediate, and if deferred, the value of the slave is taken from him and made a pledge in its place, if the debt was... The pledgee's debt. Chapter of disposition etc.: Since disposition in the pledge, injury upon it, and injury upon others is naturally subsequent to its being a pledge, he deferred it in arrangement to match the natural order. (Supplement) The pledgor's sale etc.: If the pledgee permits, it becomes effective and his right transfers to the substitute; otherwise the sale is rescinded in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). According to the three (other imams), the sale is void. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is effective, because it is a disposition in his property, so it is like manumission. The correct view is the apparent narration, because the pledgee's right has attached to it, so it cannot be effective except with his permission or repayment of the debt due to removal of the impediment. Then Shaykh Yahya remained silent about the ruling of rescission if the pledgee does not permit, indicating that it is not rescinded by his rescission. It is also said he has the right to permit and to rescind. The correct view is that it is not rescinded by his rescission, because the prohibition is for his right to avoid harm, and suspension does not harm him because his right to hold does not nullify the contract's existence without effectiveness, so it remains suspended. Then the purchaser has the option: if he wishes he may wait until the pledgor redeems the pledge, and if he wishes he may refer the matter to the judge who will rescind it, because the authority of rescission belongs to the judge, not the purchaser or the seller who is the pledgor. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/413] Then if the pledgor sells it a second time to another before the pledgee's permission, the second is also suspended. Since the first is suspended, and a suspended contract does not prevent the suspension of the second, whichever of them permits becomes effective and the other is void. And the first being suspended is restricted to when he sells it a second time to a third party; if he sells it to the pledgee, the first is rescinded. (Ayni, Fath, Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling from the matn: the pledgor's sale of the pledged property is suspended (mawquf) upon the permission of the pledgee or repayment of the debt. The commentator then explains that the chapter is placed here because the subject of disposition in the pledge is naturally subsequent to the contract of pledge. The core ruling is that the sale does not take effect immediately. If the pledgee permits, the sale becomes effective and the pledgee's right transfers to the price. If not permitted, according to Zahir al-Riwayah the sale is not automatically void but remains suspended. The 'three' (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold it is void. Abu Yusuf holds it is effective immediately because the pledgor owns the property. The correct view (sahih) is the Zahir al-Riwayah because the pledgee's right has attached. The commentator then notes that Shaykh Yahya remained silent about rescission, indicating that the sale is not rescinded by the pledgor's unilateral rescission. The purchaser has options: wait or go to judge for rescission. If a second sale occurs, both are suspended until one is permitted. The first sale is suspended only if the second sale is to a third party; if to the pledgee, the first is rescinded.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): The pledge; a contract where property is held as security for a debt.
الراهن (al-raahin): The pledgor; the debtor who gives the pledge.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The pledgee; the creditor who holds the pledge.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension; a legal status where a contract is not fully effective but not void, pending a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the pledgor's sale of the pledged property without the pledgee's permission according to Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) The sale is void (batil).
B) The sale is suspended (mawquf).
C) The sale is effective immediately.
D) The sale is revocable by the pledgor at any time.

Key Takeaway
The pledgor's sale is suspended, protecting the pledgee's right while preserving the possibility of a valid sale.
