Effectiveness of Manumission of a Pledged Slave
Ruling that the pledgor's manumission is effective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on manumission of a pledged slave and explain why it differs from sale.

Core Idea
Manumission of a pledged slave is effective immediately because it does not require delivery.

In this lesson, we examine a key difference between sale and manumission in the context of pledge. The Hanafi school holds that the pledgor's manumission is effective even without the pledgee's permission, regardless of solvency. This ruling is based on the distinction between ownership of the corpus and the pledgee's right of possession. The source passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentaries presents the ruling, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Manumission of a pledged slave by the pledgor). What is the hukm? (Effective immediately, even without pledgee's permission).
The text begins 'نفذ عتقه' meaning 'His manumission is effective'.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
What proof does the Hanafi school provide? The pledgor owns the corpus, and manumission is an act of piety. The pledgee's right is only in the hand, which follows the corpus. The text compares to manumission of a purchased slave before delivery, or an absconded slave.
The proof is based on ownership and the nature of the pledge right.
3
Follow the Shafi'i counter-argument
What is the Shafi'i position? If the pledgor is insolvent, manumission is ineffective because it nullifies the pledgee's right without compensation, similar to a suspended sale.
Shafi'i distinguishes between solvent and insolvent pledgor.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut? Sale requires delivery, which is impeded by the pledge. Manumission is a verbal act that does not require delivery, so it takes effect immediately. The pledgee can still recover the value through the slave's earnings or from the pledgor's other assets.
Hanafi response emphasizes the difference between verbal and physical acts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? According to Hanafi, the slave is free immediately and may have to earn to pay the debt. According to Shafi'i, if the pledgor is insolvent, the manumission is invalid and the slave remains in pledge.
The consequence affects the slave's status and the pledgee's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفذ عتقه: أي نفذ عتق الراهن العبد المرهون بلا إجازة المرتهن مطلقا، سواء كان موسرا أو معسرا، وقال الشافعي: لا ينفذ إن كان معسرا، وإن كان موسرا ينفذ، وهو أظهر أقواله؛ لأن في تنفيذه مع الإعسار إبطال حق المرتهن فأشبه البيع، بخلاف ما إذا كان موسرا؛ لأنه لا يبطل حقه معنى بالتضمين ولنا أنه مخاطب أعتق ملك نفسه، فلا يلغو تصرفه؛ لعدم إذن ،المرتهن كما إذا أعتق العبد المشتري قبل القبض، أو أعتق الآبق أو المغصوب، ولا خفاء في ملك الرقبة، لقيام المقتضي، وعارض الرهن لا ينبئ عن زواله، ثم إذا زال ملكه في الرقبة بإعتاقه يزول ملك المرتمن في اليد بناء عليه، كإعتاق العبد المشترك بل أولى؛ لأن ملك الرقبة أقوى من ملك اليد وامتناع النفاذ في البيع والهبة؛ لانعدام القدرة على التسليم. (مسكين، فتح) وطولب إلخ: يعني إذا كان الراهن موسرا والدين حالا طولب بأداء الدين؛ لأنه لو طولب بأداء القيمة تقع ) بقدر الدين فلا فائدة فيه الهداية : ٤٠٨/٧] ولو مؤجلا إلخ يعني لو كان الدين مؤجلا يؤخذ من المعتق قيمة العبد، وتجعل رهنا مكان العبد إذا كان موسرا؛ لأن سبب الضمان قد تحقق وفي التضمين فائدة، وهي حصول الاستيشاق من الوجه الذي بيناه، ويحبسها إلى حلول الأجل، فإذا حل اقتضاه بحقه إذا كان بجنسه؛ لأن للغريم أن يستوفي حقه من مال غريمه إذا ظفر بجنس حقه وإن كان فيه فضل رده؛ لانتهاء حكم الرهن بالاستيفاء، وإن كان أقل من رجع بالزيادة؛ لعدم ما يسقطه حقه المقاصة
ولو معسرا سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، ويرجع به على سيده، كان الراهن العبد الرهن بما سعى إذا أيسر
ولو معسرا سعى إلخ: أي لو كان الراهن معسرا سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته، ومن الدين؛ لأن حق المرتمن كان متعلقا به، وسلمت له رقبته، فإذا تعذر الرجوع على المعتق لعسرته رجع عليه؛ لأنه هو المنتفع بهذا العتق كما في عتق أحد الشريكين العبد المشترك، وكيفية ذلك أن ينظر إلى قيمة العبد يوم العتق، وإلى قيمته يوم الرهن، وإلى الدين فيستسعى في الأقل منهما. رمز الحقائق: ٤١٤/٢] فإن كان الدين أقل فالحاجة تندفع به، وإن كانت القيمة أقل فهو إنما حصل له هذا القدر، فلا تجب عليه الزيادة، وقيد المسألة في "الجوهرة" بما إذا أعتقه بغير إذن ،المرتهن وأما إذا أعتقه بإذنه فلا سعاية على العبد. (عيني، فتح)
ويرجع به إلخ : يعني إذا سعى العبد وأدى يرجع العبد بالسعاية على سيده إذا أيسر ؛ لأنه قضى دينه، وهو مضطر فيه، ولم يكن متبرعا، فصار كمعير الرهن، بخلاف العبد المستسعى إذا كان بين الشريكين، وأعتق أحدهما نصيبه والمعتق معسر، وسعى في نصيب الآخر، وأدى، بحيث لا يرجع؛ لأنه يؤدي ضمانا واجبا عليه؛ لأنه يسعى في تكميل العتق عندهما، ولتحصيل العتق عند الإمام، وهنا يسعى في ضمان على عسرة بعد تمام إعتاقه، فافترقا، فالإمام أوجب السعاية في العبد المشترك في حالتي اليسار والإعسار وفي العبد المرهون في حالة الإعسار فقط تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٣/٩]
His manumission is effective: meaning the manumission of the pledgor of the pledged slave is effective without the permission of the pledgee in all cases, whether he is solvent or insolvent. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not effective if he is insolvent, but if he is solvent it is effective, and this is the most apparent of his opinions, because carrying it out while insolvent nullifies the right of the pledgee, similar to sale, unlike if he is solvent because it does not nullify his right meaningfully due to substitution. Our proof: he is a responsible person who manumits his own property, so his disposition is not invalid due to lack of permission of the pledgee, as if he manumits a purchased slave before delivery, or manumits an absconded or usurped slave. There is no doubt in his ownership of the corpus, because the basis exists, and the impediment of pledge does not indicate its removal. Then when his ownership of the corpus is removed by his manumission, the ownership of the pledgee in the hand is removed consequent upon it, like manumission of a jointly-owned slave, even more so, because ownership of corpus is stronger than ownership of hand. And lack of effectiveness in sale and gift is due to lack of ability to deliver. (Miskin, Fath) 'And he is demanded' etc.: meaning if the pledgor is solvent and the debt is immediate, he is demanded to pay the debt, because if he were demanded to pay the value it would fall upon him to the extent of the debt, so there is no benefit. (Al-Hidayah 7:408) 'And if deferred' etc.: meaning if the debt is deferred, the value of the slave is taken from the manumitter and made a pledge in place of the slave if he is solvent, because the cause of liability has occurred, and in making him liable there is benefit, namely obtaining security from the direction we explained. He holds it until the term arrives, then when it arrives he may take his right from it if it is of the same type, because the creditor may take his right from his debtor's property if he finds the same type of his right. If there is a surplus, he returns it because the purpose of the pledge ends with satisfaction. If it is less, he returns the deficiency because there is nothing to drop his right of set-off. And if insolvent, the slave earns (by seeking means) the lesser of his value and the debt, and he has recourse to his master. The slave's earning when insolvent etc.: If the pledgor is insolvent, the slave earns the lesser of his value and the debt, because the pledgee's right was attached to him, and his corpus is surrendered to him. So when recourse to the manumitter is impossible due to his insolvency, he can have recourse to the slave because he is the one benefiting from this manumission, as in the manumission of a jointly-owned slave by one partner. The method is to consider the slave's value on the day of manumission and his value on the day of pledge and the debt, and he must earn the lesser of them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/414] If the debt is less, the need is satisfied by it; if the value is less, he only obtained this amount, so no increase is required. The matter is restricted in Al-Jawharah to when he manumits without the pledgee's permission; if he manumits with permission, there is no earning required. (Ayni, Fath) 'And he has recourse' etc.: If the slave earns and pays, the slave has recourse to his master by what he earned when the master becomes solvent, because he paid his debt involuntarily and not voluntarily, so he is like the lender of the pledge. Unlike the slave who is required to earn in the case of a jointly-owned slave when one partner manumits and is insolvent; that slave does not have recourse because he is paying a liability obligatory upon him, to complete the manumission according to them, and to attain manumission according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Here he pays a liability for insolvency after his full manumission, so they differ. Thus Imam Abu Hanifa required earning in the joint slave in both solvent and insolvent cases, but in the pledged slave only in insolvency. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/13)
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage addresses the effectiveness of the pledgor's manumission of a pledged slave. Unlike sale, manumission is effective immediately without the pledgee's permission, whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent. The commentator explains that Shafi'i differs, holding that if the pledgor is insolvent, manumission is ineffective because it nullifies the pledgee's right. The Hanafi argument is that the pledgor owns the slave's corpus, and the pledge only grants a right to hold, not ownership. Manumission removes ownership of corpus, and consequently the pledgee's right in the hand is also removed, similar to a jointly-owned slave. The text then discusses consequences: if solvent and debt due, the pledgor is demanded to pay immediately. If debt is deferred, the slave's value is taken and made a pledge. If insolvent, the slave must earn (by working) to pay the lesser of his value or the debt, and can later recover from his former master when solvent. This is contrasted with the case of a jointly-owned slave where the earning is required in both solvent and insolvent cases according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
العتق (al-itiq): Manumission; freeing a slave by the owner's declaration.
السعاية (al-saa'i): Earning by the slave through work to pay a debt or ransom; the slave is required to earn and pay it.
الموسر (al-muwsir): Solvent; having sufficient assets to pay debts.
المعسر (al-mu'sir): Insolvent; unable to pay debts due to lack of assets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the pledgor's manumission of a pledged slave when the pledgor is insolvent?
A) The manumission is ineffective because it harms the pledgee.
B) The manumission is effective and the slave is free immediately.
C) The manumission is suspended pending the pledgee's permission.
D) The manumission is effective only if the slave pays the debt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a pledgor's manumission of a pledged slave is effective immediately, even without the pledgee's permission, because manumission is a verbal act that does not require delivery, unlike sale.

Destruction of the Pledge: Liability and Substitution
Ruling on destruction by pledgor, third party, and pledgee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the liability rules when the pledged property is destroyed by the pledgor, a third party, or the pledgee, and apply the correct valuation date for each.

Core Idea
Destruction of the pledge transfers the right to its value, with the valuation date depending on who caused the destruction.

This lesson examines the three scenarios of destroying a pledged property. When the pledgor destroys it, the effect mirrors manumission. When a third party destroys it, the value becomes a new pledge. When the pledgee destroys it, the liability is based on the property's value at the time of possession, not destruction. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly resolving claims in pledge transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the destroying party
Determine who caused the destruction: pledgor, third party, or pledgee. Each has a distinct ruling.
2
Determine the liable party and the valuation date
For a third party, the value is taken at the day of destruction. For the pledgee, it is taken at the day he took possession (qabd). For the pledgor, the rule mirrors manumission.
The valuation date is critical: it determines how much is owed or becomes a pledge.
3
Apply the rule for the pledgee's liability
If the pledgee destroys, he owes the value at possession day. If the debt is deferred, he holds the value as a pledge. If the debt is due, he may satisfy his debt from the value and return any surplus.
4
Calculate the effect on the debt
When the pledgee destroys, the value at possession day is deducted from the debt. If the value is less than the debt, the remaining debt stands. If more, the surplus returns to the pledgor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإتلاف الراهن كإعتاقه وإن أتلفه أجنبي، فالمرتمن يضمنه قيمته، الأجنبي الرهن يوم هلك بما
بما سعى إذا أيسر
الرهن
الأجنبي
الرهن يوم هلك
حقه
فالمرتمن يضمنه إلخ : أي الأجنبي قيمته" أي قيمة الرهن، فتكون القيمة رهنا عنده أي عند المرتمن؛ لأنه أحق بعين الرهن حال قيامه فكذا في استرداد ما قام مقامه والواجب على هذا المستهلك قيمته . هلك باستهلاكه بخلاف ضمانه على المرتهن فإنه يعتبر قيمته يوم القبض، حتى لو كانت قيمته يوم الاستهلاك خمس مائة، ويوم الارتمان ألفا غرم خمس مائة، وكانت رهنا، وسقط من الدين خمس مائة؛ لأن المعتبر في ضمان الرهن يوم قبضه؛ لأنه به دخل في ضمانه؛ لأنه قبض استيفاء، إلا أنه يتقرر عند الهلاك، ولو استهلكه المرتهن، والدين مؤجل ضمن قیمته؛ لأنه أتلف مال الغير، وكانت رهنا في يده حتى يحل الأجل، ولو حل الدين والمضمون من جنس استوفى المرتمن منه دينه، ورد الفضل على الراهن إن كان فيه ،فضل، وإن كان دينه أكثر من قيمته رجع بالفضل، وإن نقصت القيمة بتراجع السعر إلى خمسمائة، وقد كانت يوم القبض ألفا وجبت بالاستهلاك خمس مائة، وسقط من الدين خمس مائة رمز الحقائق: ٤١٤/٢]
And the destruction by the pledgor is like his manumission. If a third party destroys it, the pledgee is made liable for its value. The third party [destroys] the pledge on the day it perished. 'The pledgee is made liable for it etc.': meaning the third party [must pay] its value, i.e. the value of the pledge, so the value becomes a pledge with him, i.e. with the pledgee, because he is more entitled to the specific pledge while it exists, so also in reclaiming what stands in its place. And the liability on this destroyer is its value at the day of destruction. Unlike his liability on the pledgee: indeed its value is considered on the day of taking possession, so that if its value on the day of destruction is five hundred and on the day of pledging it was one thousand, he pays five hundred and it becomes a pledge, and five hundred falls from the debt. Because what is considered in the liability of the pledge is the day of taking possession, because it enters his liability on that day, since it is a possessory delivery. However it is determined at the time of destruction. And if the pledgee destroys it and the debt is deferred, he is liable for its value because he destroyed the property of another, and it was a pledge in his hand until the term arrives. And if the debt falls due and the liability is of the same type, the pledgee may satisfy his debt from it and return the surplus to the pledgor if there is any. If his debt is more than its value, he may recover the deficiency. And if the value decreased due to a fall in price to five hundred, and it was one thousand on the day of taking possession, by destruction he owes five hundred, and five hundred falls from the debt. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/414]
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage covers the legal consequences of destroying the pledged property. First, if the pledgor destroys it, the ruling is the same as manumission: the pledgee's right transfers to the value (if solvent and debt due, he pays immediately; if deferred, the value becomes a new pledge; if insolvent, the slave earns, etc.). Second, if a third party destroys it, the third party must pay the value to the pledgee, and that value becomes a pledge in place of the original. The value assessed is at the time of destruction. Third, if the pledgee himself destroys it, his liability is determined by the value on the day he took possession (qabd), not the day of destruction. This is because his possession is for the purpose of recovery, so the value at the time of pledging is considered; a lower value at destruction reduces the debt proportionally. If the debt is deferred, he must pay the value and hold it as a pledge until the term.

Key Terms
الإتلاف (al-itlaf): Destruction; causing the pledged property to cease to exist, incurring liability.
القيمة (al-qeemah): The monetary value of the destroyed pledge, which becomes a substitute pledge.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability; obligation to pay compensation for destruction or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pledgee destroys the pledged property, the value for liability is determined on which day?
A) The day the pledge was first created.
B) The day of destruction.
C) The day the pledgee took possession of the pledge.
D) The day the debt was incurred.

Key Takeaway
When a pledge is destroyed, the liable party and valuation date differ: third party pays value at destruction, pledgee pays value at possession, and pledgor's destruction mirrors manumission.

Sa'yah of a Pawned Slave When Pawner Is Insolvent
Ruling and analogy on slave's work when pawner is insolvent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sa'yah for a pawned slave freed by an insolvent pawner and distinguish it from the joint-slave case using qiyas.

Core Idea
A pawned slave freed by an insolvent pawner must work to satisfy the mortgagee, then recoup from the pawner.

When a pawner (raahn) frees a pawned slave without the mortgagee's permission and is insolvent, the slave's freedom is valid but the mortgagee's right remains attached. The slave must work (perform sa'yah) to pay off the lesser of his value or the debt, and later reclaim from the pawner when he becomes solvent. This ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to the case of two partners freeing a jointly owned slave, but with a key difference in recourse. This lesson dissects the ruling, its proof, and the subtle distinctions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (paigner frees pawned slave while insolvent) and the hukm: the slave must work for the lesser of value or debt, and has recourse.
This is the core rule from the matn: 'ولو معسرا سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، ويرجع به على سيده'.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is sa'yah obligatory? Because the mortgagee's right (haqq al-murtahin) was attached to the slave, and the pawner benefits from the freeing.
The slave is compelled, not a volunteer.
3
Examine the qiyas (analogy)
The text compares to the case of one partner freeing a jointly-owned slave while insolvent. In both cases, another party has a right in the slave. Identify the asl (joint slave), far (pawned slave), and illa (attachment of another's right).
Qiyas used: 'كما في عتق أحد الشريكين العبد المشترك'.
4
Identify the distinction (tafriq)
Though analogous, the two cases differ on recourse. In the joint slave case, the slave works to complete freedom and has no recourse; in the pawned slave case, the slave is already fully free and works only due to insolvency, so he has recourse. Understand the reason: in joint slave, the payment is obligatory (daman wajib); here it is due to constraint.
Key phrase: 'بخلاف العبد المستسعى... بحيث لا يرجع لأنه يؤدي ضمانا واجبا عليه'.
5
Note the condition and Imam's position
The sa'yah is only required if the pawner freed without the mortgagee's permission. If with permission, no sa'yah. Also, Imam Abu Hanifa obliges sa'yah in the joint slave in both solvency/insolvency, but only in pawned slave when pawner is insolvent.
This condition is from al-Jawharah: 'قيد المسألة في الجوهرة بما إذا أعتقه بغير إذن المرتهن'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو معسرا سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، ويرجع به على سيده. ولو معسرا سعى إلخ: أي لو كان الراهن معسرا سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته، ومن الدين؛ لأن حق المرتمن كان متعلقا به، وسلمت له رقبته، فإذا تعذر الرجوع على المعتق لعسرته رجع عليه؛ لأنه هو المنتفع بهذا العتق كما في عتق أحد الشريكين العبد المشترك، وكيفية ذلك أن ينظر إلى قيمة العبد يوم العتق، وإلى قيمته يوم الرهن، وإلى الدين فيستسعى في الأقل منهما. رمز الحقائق: ٤١٤/٢] فإن كان الدين أقل فالحاجة تندفع به، وإن كانت القيمة أقل فهو إنما حصل له هذا القدر، فلا تجب عليه الزيادة، وقيد المسألة في "الجوهرة" بما إذا أعتقه بغير إذن المرتهن وأما إذا أعتقه بإذنه فلا سعاية على العبد. (عيني، فتح) ويرجع به إلخ : يعني إذا سعى العبد وأدى يرجع العبد بالسعاية على سيده إذا أيسر ؛ لأنه قضى دينه، وهو مضطر فيه، ولم يكن متبرعا، فصار كمعير الرهن، بخلاف العبد المستسعى إذا كان بين الشريكين، وأعتق أحدهما نصيبه والمعتق معسر، وسعى في نصيب الآخر، وأدى، بحيث لا يرجع؛ لأنه يؤدي ضمانا واجبا عليه؛ لأنه يسعى في تكميل العتق عندهما، ولتحصيل العتق عند الإمام، وهنا يسعى في ضمان على عسرة بعد تمام إعتاقه، فافترقا، فالإمام أوجب السعاية في العبد المشترك في حالتي اليسار والإعسار وفي العبد المرهون في حالة الإعسار فقط تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٣/٩]
And if he is insolvent, the slave works for the lesser of his value and the debt, and he has recourse against his master for it. And the explanation: i.e. if the pawner is insolvent, the slave works for the lesser of his value and the debt, because the right of the mortgagee was attached to him, and his body is free, so when recourse against the freeer is impossible due to his insolvency, he has recourse against him because he is the one benefiting from this freeing, as in the case of one of two partners freeing a jointly owned slave. The manner is: look at the value of the slave on the day of freeing, and his value on the day of pawning, and the debt; then he works for the lesser of them. If the debt is less, the need is satisfied by it; if the value is less, that is what he obtained, so no increase is obligatory. The issue is restricted in al-Jawharah to when he freed him without the mortgagee's permission; as for if he freed him with his permission, there is no sa'yah on the slave. He has recourse: i.e. when the slave works and pays, he has recourse against his master for the sa'yah when he becomes solvent, because he paid his debt, and he was compelled in it, and he was not a volunteer, so it is like a borrower of the pawn. Unlike the slave working when between two partners, and one frees his share and the freeer is insolvent, and he works for the other's share and pays, such that he does not have recourse, because he pays an obligatory guarantee, because he works to complete the freeing according to them, and to obtain freedom according to Imam. Here he works for a guarantee due to insolvency after his complete freeing, so they differ. So Imam made sa'yah obligatory in the jointly-owned slave in both states of solvency and insolvency, and in the mortgaged slave only in insolvency.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary explaining the sa'yah of a pawned slave freed by an insolvent pawner. The ruling: the slave must work to pay the lesser of his value or the debt, and can later reclaim from the pawner when he becomes solvent. The commentary provides the rationale: the mortgagee's right is attached to the slave, the pawner benefits from freeing, and the slave is compelled. It analogizes to the case of a joint slave freed by one partner, but distinguishes: in the joint case, the slave works to complete freedom and does not have recourse; here, the slave is already fully free and works only due to insolvency, so he has recourse. Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that sa'yah is obligatory in the joint slave in both solvency and insolvency, but only in insolvency for the pawned slave. The passage guides the calculation: compare values and debt, take the lesser. It also specifies that if the pawner freed with the mortgagee's permission, there is no sa'yah.

Key Terms
السعاية (al-sa'yah): The slave's work to earn money to pay off a debt or value
المعسر (al-mu'sir): The person who is insolvent, cannot pay debts
العتق (al-'itq): Freeing a slave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever the pawner frees the slave, regardless of solvency.
B) Only when the pawner frees the slave with the mortgagee's permission and is insolvent.
C) Only when the pawner frees the slave without the mortgagee's permission and is insolvent.
D) Only when the pawner frees the slave without permission and is solvent.

Key Takeaway
The pawned slave freed by an insolvent pawner must work for the lesser of his value or the debt, and can reclaim from the pawner later.

Destruction of Pawn by Pawner and Third Party
Rulings on destruction of pawn by different parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the consequences of destroying a pawn depending on who destroys it (pawner, mortgagee, or third party) and apply the Hanafi rules for valuation and substitution.

Core Idea
Destruction by pawner equals freeing; by third party, value substitutes for pawn; mortgagee's destruction may be collection.

In pawn (rahn) transactions, the pawn remains the property of the pawner but is held as security. What happens if the pawn is destroyed? The ruling depends on who destroys it: the pawner, the mortgagee, or a third party. This lesson, from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains the Hanafi position in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the destroyer
Determine whether the pawn is destroyed by the pawner, the mortgagee, or a third party. Each has a distinct legal consequence.
The destroyer's relationship to the pawn determines the ruling.
2
Apply the analogy to freeing for pawner
The pawner's destruction is treated like freeing (itq): he must pay the value immediately if debt is due, or substitute it as a new pawn if debt is deferred.
The difference from freeing is that no sa'yah (compulsory labor) is required from the owner.
3
Handle third party destruction
If a third party destroys the pawn, the mortgagee is entitled to claim its value (at consumption) from the third party. That value becomes a new pawn in place of the destroyed item.
The mortgagee does not lose his security; the value substitutes for the pawn.
4
Analyze valuation and debt impact
For the mortgagee's guarantee, value is assessed at the time of possession. If the consumption value is less than the possession value, the shortfall is deducted from the debt. For third party, liability is based on consumption value.
The example in the text clarifies: if possession value 1000 and consumption value 500, the third party pays 500, which becomes pawn, and 500 drops from the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإتلاف الراهن كإعتاقه وإن أتلفه أجنبي، فالمرتمن يضمنه قيمته. وإتلاف الراهن إلخ: يعني إنه إذا أتلفه وهو موسر والدين حال أدى القيمة في الحال، وإن كان مؤجلا أدى القيمة وجعلت رهنا مكانه حتى يحل الدين. والحاصل أن إتلاف الراهن كإعتاقه في الأحكام المذكورة، إلا أنه لا سعاية هنا؛ لاستحالة وجوبها على المالك، وقيد المسألة بإتلاف الراهن؛ لأنه لو أتلفه المرتهن والدين حال يكون مستوفيا، وإلا تؤخذ قيمته منه وتجعل رهنا. فالمرتمن يضمنه إلخ: أي الأجنبي قيمته، أي قيمة الرهن، فتكون القيمة رهنا عنده أي عند المرتمن؛ لأنه أحق بعين الرهن حال قيامه فكذا في استرداد ما قام مقامه. والواجب على هذا المستهلك قيمته. هلك باستهلاكه بخلاف ضمانه على المرتمن فإنه يعتبر قيمته يوم القبض، حتى لو كانت قيمته يوم الاستهلاك خمس مائة، ويوم الارتمان ألفا غرم خمس مائة، وكانت رهنا، وسقط من الدين خمس مائة؛ لأن المعتبر في ضمان الرهن يوم قبضه؛ لأنه به دخل في ضمانه؛ لأنه قبض استيفاء، إلا أنه يتقرر عند الهلاك. ولو استهلكه المرتهن، والدين مؤجل ضمن قيمته؛ لأنه أتلف مال الغير، وكانت رهنا في يده حتى يحل الأجل. ولو حل الدين والمضمون من جنس استوفى المرتمن منه دينه، ورد الفضل على الراهن إن كان فيه فضل، وإن كان دينه أكثر من قيمته رجع بالفضل، وإن نقصت القيمة بتراجع السعر إلى خمسمائة، وقد كانت يوم القبض ألفا وجبت بالاستهلاك خمس مائة، وسقط من الدين خمس مائة. فتكون رهنا عنده.
And destruction by the pawner is like his freeing, and if a third party destroys it, the mortgagee is liable for its value. And [the commentary] 'destruction by the pawner etc.' means: if he destroys it while solvent and the debt is due, he pays the value immediately; if the debt is deferred, he pays the value and it becomes a pawn in place of it until the debt is due. The summary: destruction by the pawner is like his freeing in the mentioned rulings, except that there is no sa'yah here because it cannot be obligatory on the owner. The issue is restricted to destruction by the pawner; because if the mortgagee destroys it and the debt is due, he is considered to have collected it; otherwise, its value is taken from him and made a pawn. 'The mortgagee is liable for it etc.' means: the third party [is liable for] its value, i.e. the value of the pawn, so the value becomes a pawn with him, i.e. with the mortgagee, because he has more right to the pawn itself while it exists, so likewise in recovering what stands in its place. The liability on this consumer (the third party) is its value. It is destroyed by his consumption, unlike the guarantee on the mortgagee: it is considered at its value on the day of taking possession, even if its value on the day of consumption is five hundred and on the day of taking possession was one thousand; he pays five hundred, and it is a pawn, and five hundred drops from the debt. Because the consideration in the guarantee of the pawn is the day of taking possession; because by it he entered into its guarantee, because it is a taking of collection, except that it is established at the time of destruction. And if the mortgagee consumes it while the debt is deferred, he is liable for its value because he destroyed another's property, and it was a pawn in his hand until the term comes. And if the debt is due and the guaranteed item is of the same genus, the mortgagee collects his debt from it, and returns the surplus to the pawner if there is surplus; if his debt is more than its value, he claims the surplus; and if the value decreases due to price fluctuation to five hundred, and it was one thousand on the day of taking possession, the liability for consumption is five hundred, and five hundred drops from the debt. So it becomes a pawn with him.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios of destruction of the pawn. First, if the pawner destroys it, it is like freeing: he must pay the value immediately (if debt due) or it becomes a substitute pawn (if deferred). Unlike freeing, there is no sa'yah because the owner cannot be obligated to work. Second, if a third party destroys it, the mortgagee is entitled to the value from the third party, and that value becomes a new pawn with the mortgagee. The commentary explains that the value is assessed at the time of the mortgagee's taking possession, not at destruction, for the purpose of guarantee. Examples illustrate: if value at possession is 1000 and at destruction 500, the mortgagee receives 500 and 500 drops from the debt. If the mortgagee himself destroys it, different rules apply: if debt due, it is considered collection; if deferred, he is liable for the value and it remains a pawn. The passage concludes that the value becomes a pawn with the mortgagee.

Key Terms
إتلاف (itlaf): Destruction or consumption of the pawn
الضمان (al-daman): Liability or guarantee; responsibility for the value of the pawn
قيمة الرهن (qimat al-rahn): The monetary value of the pawned item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The third party pays the pawner directly.
B) The mortgagee is liable for the value and it becomes a new pawn.
C) The pawn is simply lost and the debt extinguishes.
D) The pawner must find a replacement.

Key Takeaway
Destruction of pawn triggers a substitute liability: the destroyer must pay the value, which becomes a new pawn for the mortgagee, with valuation rules depending on the destroyer's status.

Lending the Pawn Back: Effect on Guarantee
Rulings on the mortgagee lending the pawn back to the pawner or to a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of the mortgagee lending the pawn back to the pawner on the guarantee and explain when the guarantee returns.

Core Idea
Lending the pawn back removes guarantee, but the pawn contract remains; guarantee returns upon repossession.

Mortgagees often need to return the pawn to the owner temporarily. This lesson examines the legal consequences on the mortgagee's liability (daman) and the status of the pawn contract. We will explore the rule and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The mortgagee lends the pawn to the pawner. The ruling is that the mortgagee's guarantee is removed. State the hukm level (mubah) and its consequence.
The act is permissible, but it has legal effects.
2
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The guarantee was based on possession (yad daman). By returning possession to the owner, the basis is gone, so guarantee is lifted.
If the pawn is destroyed with the pawner, it is destroyed free of liability.
3
Consider the return of guarantee
If the mortgagee takes back possession of the pawn, the guarantee returns because possession is regained.
The pawn contract remains valid; only guarantee is temporarily removed.
4
Examine lending to a third party
If either party lends to a third party with the other's permission, guarantee also falls. Both parties may demand return as pawn.
Lending to a third party without permission may have different rulings.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on leasing
There is a difference of opinion on whether the mortgagee can lease the pawn. Al-Isbijahbi holds it valid but voids the pawn; others disagree. This lesson focuses on lending, not leasing.
The source text mentions this ikhtilaf but does not resolve it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج من ضمانه بإعارته من راهنه فلو هلك في يد الراهن بعد الإعارة يهلك مجانا وبرجوعه عاد ضمانه ولو أعاره أحدهما أجنبيا بإذن الآخر سقط الضمان، ولكل أن يرده رهنا، من الراهن والمرتمن الرهن الراهن أو المرتمن وخرج من ضمانه إلخ يعني إذا أعار المرتمن الرهن من الراهن يخرج من ضمان المرتمن؛ لأن الضمان كان باعتبار قبضه، وقد انتقض بالرد إلى صاحبه فيرتفع بالضمان تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥/٩] ولو أذن الراهن المرتهن في استعماله، وإعارته للعمل، فهلك قبل العمل أو بعد الفراغ منه هلك بالدين؛ لبقاء عقد الرهن، ولو هلك في حالة العمل والاستعمال هلك أمانة؛ لثبوت يد العارية حينئذ. (فتح) يهلك مجانا إلخ: أي بلا بدل، يعني لا يصير المرتهن مستوفيا دينه؛ لفوات القبض الموجب للضمان، حتى لو كان أعطاه به كفيلا لم يلزم الكفيل شيء لخروجه من الرهن، نعم لو كان أخذه بغير رضا المرتهن جاز ضمان الكفيل. (فتح) عاد إلخ : يعني برجوع الرهن إلى يد المرتمن عاد الضمان حتى يذهب الدين بهلاكه، لعود القبض الموجب للضمان، وللمرتهن أن يسترده إلى يده؛ لأن عقد الرهن باق إلا في حق الضمان في تلك الحالة ولهذا لو مات الراهن قبل أن يسترده كان المرتهن أحق به من سائر غرمائه؛ لأن يد العارية ليست بلازمة، والضمان ليس من لوازم الرهن؛ لأنه قد ينفك عنه، ألا ترى أن ولد الرهن رهن وليس بمضمون تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥/٩] ولو أعاره أحدهما إلخ أي أعار الرهن الراهن أو المرتمن، وفي استعمال لفظ الإعارة في جانب المرتمن تسامح؛ لأن الإعارة تمليك المنافع بغير عوض، وهو لم يكن مالكا فكيف يملك تمليكها ولكن لما عومل ههنا معاملة الإعارة من عدم الضمان، وتمكن الاسترداد، أطلق اسم الإعارة؛ لمنافاة بين يد العارية ويد الرهن. (فتح) سقط الضمان أي سقط الضمان من المرتمن؛ لما ذكرنا أن الضمان كان باعتبار قبضه، وقد انتقض. ولكل أن يرده إلخ: أي لكل واحد من الراهن والمرتمن أن يرده على حاله رهنا من غير عقد جديد؛ لبقائه على الرهنية، وخص الإعارة؛ لأنه إذا آجره، أو باعه أو وهبه أحدهما من أجنبي، أو من المرتهن بإذن الآخر يخرج عن الرهن، ولا يعود رهنا إلا بعقد جديد، ولهذا لو مات الراهن قبل الرد إلى المرتمن يكون المرتهن أسوة للغرماء، كذا في "ملا مسكين" و"العيني؛ قال في "الفتح": فهذا الكلام صريح في جواز الإجارة من المرتهن، قال الإسبيحابي: لو استأجره المرتمن صحت الإجارة وبطل الرهن إذا جدد القبض للإجارة، ولو هلك في يده قبل انقضاء مدة الإجارة أو بعد انقضائها، ولم يحبسه عن الراهن هلك أمانة ولا يذهب بهلاكه شيء من الدين، ولو حبسه عن الراهن بعد انقضاء مدة الإجارة صار غاصبا، انتهى ويخالفه ما في معراج" "الدراية" حيث قال: ولو آجره الراهن من المرتمن كانت باطلة، وهو بمنزلة ما لو أعاره أو أودعه، وفي "الإيضاح : آجره من المرتمن خرج من الرهن، و لم يعد إلى الرهن أبدا؛ لأن الإجارة عقد لازم، فإذا لزم العقد انتفى الرهن.
And it leaves his guarantee by his lending it to its owner, so if it is destroyed in the hand of the pawner after the loan, it is destroyed free (of liability), and by its return, his guarantee returns. And if one of them lends it to a third party with the permission of the other, the guarantee falls, and each may return it as a pawn. 'And it leaves his guarantee etc.' means: when the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pawner, it leaves the guarantee of the mortgagee, because the guarantee was based on his possession, and it is annulled by returning to its owner, so the guarantee is lifted. And if the pawner permits the mortgagee to use it and lend it for work, and it is destroyed before work or after finishing, it is destroyed against the debt due to the continuing pawn contract; but if it is destroyed during work and use, it is destroyed as a trust due to the hand of loan at that time. 'Destroyed free' i.e. without compensation, meaning the mortgagee does not become satisfied for his debt due to loss of possession that necessitates guarantee; even if he had given a guarantor, the guarantor is not liable because it left the pawn. Yes, if he took it without the mortgagee's consent, the guarantor's guarantee is valid. 'And by its return his guarantee returns' means by the return of the pawn to the hand of the mortgagee, the guarantee returns so that the debt is extinguished by its destruction, due to the return of possession that necessitates guarantee. And the mortgagee may reclaim it to his hand because the pawn contract remains except regarding guarantee in that state; therefore if the pawner dies before reclaiming, the mortgagee has priority over other creditors because the loan hand is not binding, and guarantee is not necessary for pawn; it may be separate. And if one of them lends it i.e. the pawner or mortgagee lends the pawn; and the use of the word 'loan' for the mortgagee is lax because loan is giving ownership of benefits without compensation, and he is not the owner so how can he give ownership? But because it is treated here like loan regarding absence of guarantee and possibility of return, the name loan is used due to incompatibility between loan hand and pawn hand. 'The guarantee falls' i.e. the guarantee falls from the mortgagee because, as mentioned, the guarantee was based on his possession and it is annulled. 'And each may return it' i.e. each of the pawner and mortgagee may return it in its state as a pawn without a new contract due to its remaining as pawn. This is specific to loan because if one of them leases it, sells it, or gives it as a gift to a third party or to the mortgagee with the other's permission, it leaves the pawn and does not return as a pawn except with a new contract. Therefore if the pawner dies before returning to the mortgagee, the mortgagee is like other creditors. This statement clearly permits lease from the mortgagee. Al-Isbijahbi said: if the mortgagee leases it, the lease is valid and the pawn is invalidated if possession is renewed for the lease; if it is destroyed in his hand before or after the lease period and he does not detain it from the pawner, it is destroyed as a trust and nothing of the debt is extinguished; if he detains it after the period, he becomes a usurper. This conflicts with what is in Miraj al-Dirayah where it is said: if the pawner leases it from the mortgagee, it is invalid and is like if he lent it or deposited it. In al-Idah: he leased it from the mortgagee, it leaves the pawn and never returns because lease is a binding contract; when the contract is binding, the pawn ceases.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of 'i'arah' (lending) the pawn back to the pawner or to a third party. When the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pawner, the mortgagee's guarantee (daman) is removed because possession returns to the owner. If the pawn is then destroyed with the pawner, it is without liability. If the mortgagee takes it back, guarantee returns. If either party lends to a third party with the other's permission, guarantee also falls, and both parties can demand its return as a pawn. The commentary delves into nuances: if the pawner permits the mortgagee to use or lend the pawn, and it is destroyed during use, it is a trust (amanah) not subject to guarantee. The discussion also touches on renting the pawn: there is a difference of opinion on the validity of the mortgagee renting the pawn and the effects on the pawn contract. The passage concludes with a note that the term 'i'arah' is used loosely for the mortgagee because he is not the owner, but the legal effect is similar.

Key Terms
الإعارة (al-i'arah): Lending something for use without compensation
الضمان (al-daman): The mortgagee's liability for the pawn due to possession
يد العارية (yad al-'ariyah): Hand of loan; possession as a borrower, which is a trust (amanah) without liability for destruction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the mortgagee's guarantee when he lends the pawn back to the pawner?
A) The guarantee remains unchanged.
B) The guarantee is permanently removed.
C) The guarantee is removed but returns if the pawn is returned to the mortgagee.
D) The pawn contract is voided.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's guarantee is based on possession; lending the pawn back relinquishes possession and thus guarantee, but the pawn contract remains intact.

Mortgagee Lending the Pawn to the Pledgor: Effect on Liability
Explains the effect of mortgagee lending pawn back to pledgor on liability and pawn status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pledgor and explain how liability changes based on possession.

Core Idea
Lending the pawn to the pledgor removes liability but does not cancel the pawn contract.

When a pawn (rahn) is given as security, the mortgagee (murtahim) holds it as a trust with liability (daman). But what happens if the mortgagee lends the pawn back to the pledgor (rahin)? This lesson unpacks the legal effect: the pawn remains a pledge, but the mortgagee's liability drops. We will also explore the related dispute on the mortgagee hiring the pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mortgagee lending the pawn to the pledgor. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) as a transaction that removes the mortgagee's liability but keeps the pawn intact as security.
The pawn does not return to the pledgor as if the loan were cancelled; it remains a pledge in the mortgagee's right.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is aqli (rational): liability (daman) was attached to possession (qabd). By returning possession to the owner, the basis for liability is invalidated. The text cites 'because the liability was based on his possession, and it is invalidated by returning it to its owner'.
This is a clear example of causation by possession – the reason for liability is the mortgagee's hand (yad daman).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection between possession and liability is direct: the mortgagee is only liable because the pawn is in his custody. Once he relinquishes custody, liability ceases. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh: 'al-daman bi al-yad' (liability is by hand).
Contrast with the case where the pawn is lost in the mortgagee's hand – then it is guaranteed against his debt.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on hiring
The text reports a dispute about the mortgagee hiring the pawn from the pledgor. One view (Al-Ispijabi, Al-Fath) says hire is valid and voids the pawn if new possession is taken; the other (Miraj al-Diraya, Al-Iydah) says hire is void and the pawn remains.
This dispute highlights the tension between the mortgagee's right to benefit and the pawn's function as security.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later fatwa compilations is the permissibility of the mortgagee hiring the pawn from the pledgor. This view is preferred because it respects the mutual agreement and does not conflict with the pawn's core purpose.
The tarjih authority is drawn from Al-Fath and the fatwa tradition.

Source Text

(فتح) سقط الضمان أي سقط الضمان من المرتمن؛ لما ذكرنا أن الضمان كان باعتبار قبضه، وقد انتقض. ولكل أن يرده إلخ: أي لكل واحد من الراهن والمرتمن أن يرده على حاله رهنا من غير عقد جديد؛ لبقائه على الرهنية، وخص الإعارة؛ لأنه إذا آجره، أو باعه أو وهبه أحدهما من أجنبي، أو من المرتهن بإذن الآخر يخرج عن الرهن، ولا يعود رهنا إلا بعقد جديد، ولهذا لو مات الراهن قبل الرد إلى المرتمن يكون المرتهن أسوة للغرماء، كذا في "ملا مسكين" و"العيني؛ قال في "الفتح": فهذا الكلام صريح في جواز الإجارة من المرتهن، قال الإسبيحابي: لو استأجره المرتمن صحت الإجارة وبطل الرهن إذا جدد القبض للإجارة، ولو هلك في يده قبل انقضاء مدة الإجارة أو بعد انقضائها، ولم يحبسه عن الراهن هلك أمانة ولا يذهب بهلاكه شيء من الدين، ولو حبسه عن الراهن بعد انقضاء مدة الإجارة صار غاصبا، انتهى ويخالفه ما في معراج الدراية حيث قال: ولو آجره الراهن من المرتمن كانت باطلة، وهو بمنزلة ما لو أعاره أو أودعه، وفي الإيضاح : آجره من المرتمن خرج من الرهن، و لم يعد إلى الرهن أبدا؛ لأن الإجارة عقد لازم، فإذا لزم العقد انتفى الرهن.
So it becomes a pledge with him and leaves his liability by his lending it to the pledgor. So if it perishes in the hand of the pledgor after the lending, it perishes without compensation. And if it returns, his liability returns. And if one of them lends it to a stranger with the permission of the other, the liability drops, and each may return it as a pledge, from the pledgor and the mortgagee. Commentary: Means when the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pledgor, it leaves the mortgagee's liability; because the liability was based on his possession, and it is invalidated by returning it to its owner, so the liability is removed. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 15/9) And if the pledgor permits the mortgagee to use it and lend it for work, and it perishes before work or after finishing it, it perishes against the debt because the pawn contract remains; if it perishes during work and use, it perishes as a trust because the hand of loan is established then. (Fath) It perishes without compensation etc.: meaning without a substitute; means the mortgagee does not become satisfied of his debt because the possession that necessitates liability has been missed; even if he had given a guarantor for it, the guarantor is not liable because it left the pawn; yes, if he took it without the mortgagee's consent, the guarantor's guarantee is valid. (Fath) Returns etc.: means by the pawn returning to the hand of the mortgagee, the liability returns so that the debt is extinguished by its perishing, due to the return of the possession that necessitates liability, and the mortgagee may take it back to his hand because the pawn contract remains except regarding liability in that state; thus if the pledgor dies before he retrieves it, the mortgagee has priority over other creditors because the hand of loan is not binding and liability is not a necessary concomitant of pawn; for it may be separated from it; do you not see that the offspring of a pawn is a pledge but not guaranteed? (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 15/9). And if one of them lends it etc.: means the pledgor or mortgagee lends the pawn; in using the term 'lending' regarding the mortgagee there is tolerance because lending is granting benefits without compensation, and he is not an owner so how can he grant ownership? But since it is treated here like lending regarding lack of liability and possibility of retrieval, the term is used loosely; because there is inconsistency between the hand of loan and the hand of pawn. (Fath) Liability drops: i.e., liability drops from the mortgagee; due to what we mentioned that liability was based on his possession, which is invalidated. And each may return it etc.: i.e., each of the pledgor and mortgagee may return it as a pledge in its state without a new contract, because it remains in pawn status. And the exception is lending; because if he hires it, sells it, or gifts it, one of them from a stranger or from the mortgagee with the other's permission, it leaves the pawn and does not return as a pawn except with a new contract; thus if the pledgor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, the mortgagee is like the other creditors. (from Mulla Miskin and al-'Aini. In al-Fath: This statement is explicit in permitting hiring from the mortgagee. Al-Ispijabi said: If the mortgagee hires it, the hire is valid and the pawn is void if he renews possession for the hire; and if it perishes in his hand before expiry of the hire period or after it, and he does not detain it from the pledgor, it perishes as a trust and nothing of the debt is discharged; if he detains it from the pledgor after expiry, he becomes a usurper. End. And it is opposed by what is in Miraj al-Diraya where it says: If the pledgor hires it to the mortgagee, it is void, and it is like lending or depositing. And in al-Iydah: He hired it to the mortgagee, it leaves the pawn and never returns to pawn because hire is a binding contract; when the contract becomes binding, the pawn is void.)
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a teaching on the effect of the mortgagee (murtahim) lending the pawn (rahn) back to the pledgor (rahin). The base ruling states that when the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pledgor, the pawn leaves the mortgagee's liability (daman) but remains a pledge. The liability was based on possession (qabd), and by returning the item to its owner, that possession is invalidated. So if the pawn perishes in the pledgor's hands, it is lost as a trust (amanah) – the mortgagee does not lose his debt, nor does the pledgor owe compensation for the pawn. This is the wisdom of not making the mortgagee liable: the debt remains, and the pawn's value does not substitute it. However, if the pawn returns to the mortgagee's possession, liability returns. The text then covers the case of lending to a third party with both parties' permission: liability drops, and either the pledgor or mortgagee may retake the pawn back to the original state without a new contract. An important discussion arises regarding hiring (ijara) the pawn to the mortgagee. According to one view (from al-Fath and al-Ispijabi), the mortgagee hiring the pawn from the pledgor is valid. The hire contract supersedes the pawn: the mortgagee takes new possession as a hirer, and the pawn contract is void. If the item perishes, it is an amanah (no liability for the debt). The opposing view (from Miraj al-Diraya and al-Iydah) considers such hiring void because the mortgagee cannot be both owner of the benefit and holder of the pawn simultaneously; they argue the pawn either remains or is void but cannot be reinstated. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the permissibility view. This disagreement is a intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the student should know the practical consequence: if valid, the mortgagee can use the pawn without liability for the debt; if invalid, the pawn remains and the hire is null.

Key Terms
إعارة (i'arah): Loan for use without compensation; here applied metaphorically to the mortgagee's act of giving the pawn to the pledgor for use, even though the mortgagee is not the owner, due to the special treatment of pawn.
ضمان (daman): Liability for loss; the mortgagee's liability for the pawn if lost in his possession.
قبض (qabd): Possession; here the basis for liability in pawn contracts.
إجارة (ijara): Hiring contract; the mortgagee hiring the pawn from the pledgor is a disputed issue within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee (murtahim) lends the pawn (rahn) to the pledgor (rahin) and it is lost in the pledgor's hands, what is the effect on the debt?
A) The debt is discharged because the pawn is lost.
B) The mortgagee's debt remains, and the pledgor owes no compensation to the mortgagee for the pawn.
C) The mortgagee loses his debt because he lent it voluntarily.
D) The pledgor must pay the mortgagee the value of the pawn.

Key Takeaway
Lending the pawn to the pledgor removes the mortgagee's liability but keeps the pawn contract intact; the mortgagee can reclaim the pawn at any time.

Borrowing a Garment to Pledge It: Validity and Conditions
Rules for borrowing an item specifically for pawning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on borrowing a garment to pawn it and apply the Hanafi rule that violating the lender's specification creates liability for both the borrower and the mortgagee.

Core Idea
Borrowing for pawning is valid; violating the lender's specification makes both borrower and mortgagee liable.

This lesson deals with a specific case of borrowing (isti'arah) where the purpose is to pawn the item. The Hanafi school validates this arrangement based on a qiyas of granting possession, and also explains the consequences when the borrower ignores the lender's conditions regarding the amount, type, or place of pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The base text states: 'If he borrows a garment to pawn it, it is valid.' Identify the act (isti'arah with a specific purpose) and the hukm level (sahih/valid).
2
Understand the qiyas reasoning
The commentary explains that the validity is based on qiyas: the lender grants possession (yad) to the mortgagee without ownership, analogous to granting full ownership in a sale with option (bai' bi al-khiyar). Possession can be separated from ownership.
This is a clear example of qiyas jaliyy (clear analogy).
3
Note the effect of specification
If the lender specifies the amount, type of item, or place to pawn, and the borrower violates that condition, the lender has a choice (khiyar) to hold the borrower (musta'ir) or the mortgagee (murtahim) liable for the garment's value. Both are considered transgressors.
Specification is meaningful because it protects the lender's interests.
4
Determine the compensation
The garment is qimi (non-fungible), so compensation is its market value (qimah), not a like item (mithl). The commentator explicitly rejects the statement 'wajaba mithlahu' as incorrect.
This distinction matters in calculating damages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استعار ثوبا ليرهنه صح، ولو عين قدرا أو جنسا أو بلدا فخالف ضمن المعير المعير أي قدر ما يرهنه أي جنس ما يرهنه يرهن فيه المستعير الراهن المستعير أو المرتهن، وإن وافق وهلك عند المرتمن صار مستوفيا، ضمن المعير المستعير فيما قيده المرتمن لدينه صح إلخ: أي صح الاستعارة والرهن؛ لأن المعير متبرع بإثبات ملك اليد للمرتهن، فيقاس التبرع بملك اليد وحده على التبرع بإثبات ملك العين واليد جميعا، ويجوز أن ينفصل ملك اليد عن ملك العين ثبوتا للمرتهن كما ينفصل زوالا في حق البائع إذا باع بشرط الخيار ، ثم يكون الثوب المستعار رهنا بما رهن ،به قليلا كان أو كثيرا إذا أطلق، ولم يقيده بشيء؛ لأن الإطلاق تجب اعتباره خصوصا في الإعارة؛ لأن الجهالة فيها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة. (عيني، فتح) ضمن المعير إلخ: أي إذا عين معير الثوب قدر ما يرهن الثوب به، أو عين جنس ما يرهن به، أو عين بلدا يرهن فيه، فخالف المستعير الراهن المعير كان للمعير الخيار إن شاء ضمن المستعير، وإن شاء ضمن عما عينه أيضا؛ لأن غرض المعير أن يضير المرتمن مستوفيا للأكثر بمقابلته عند الهلاك، ليرجع عليه بالكثير، والنقصان عما عين يمنع ذلك؛ لأنه إذا رهنه بأقل، فعند الهلاك إنما يرجع المعير على المستعير بذلك القدر، فلم يحصل فصار متعديا، فيضمن، إلا إذا عين له أكثر من قيمته فرهنه بأقل من ذلك بمثل قيمته أو أكثر لا يضمن؛ لأنه خلاف إلى خير؛ لأن غرضه من الرجوع عليه بأكثر حاصل بذلك مع تيسر أدائه . قال في "الذخيرة" وغيرها : لو سمى له شيئا فرهنه بأقل أو أكثر فهو على ثلاثة أوجه الأول: أن تكون قيمة الثوب مثل الدين المسمى، الثاني: أن تكون أكثر منه، وفيما إذا رهن بأكثر من الدين أو بأقل يضمن قيمته، الثالث: أن تكون أقل منه، فإن زاد على المسمى ضمن القيمة وإن نقص فإن كان النقصان إلى تمام قيمة الثوب لا يضمن، وإن إلى أقل ضمن قيمته ومثل التقييد بالقيمة التقييد بالجنس والشخص والبلد؛ لأن كل ذلك مفيد؛ لتيسر بعض الأجناس في التحصيل دون البعض، وتفاوت الأشخاص والبلدان في الحفظ والأمانة، فيضمن بالمخالفة. ثم إن ضمن المعير المستعير تم عقد الرهن بينه وبين الراهن؛ لأنه ملكه بأداء الضمان فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه، وإن ضمن المرتمن رجع المرتمن بما ضمن، وبالدين على الراهن على ما بيناه في الاستحقاق. هذا ملخص ما في الشروح وغيرها فاغتنمه واحفظه. صار مستوفيا إلخ لأن قبض الرهن قبض استيفاء، وبالهلاك يتم الاستيفاء فيسقط الدين عن الراهن، ويضمن للمعير قيمته؛ لأنه قضى بذلك القدر دينه إن كان كله مضمونا وإلا يضمن قدر المضمون والباقي أمانة، وهذا ظاهر، وكذا لو نقصت قيمة الرهن بعيب أصابه يذهب من الدين بحسابه، ويرجع المعير بذلك على الراهن؛ لما ذكرنا وقول المؤلف: ووجب مثله ليس بظاهر؛ لأن الثوب من القيمي لا من المثلي، وقول ملا" "مسكين أي وجب مثل الدين للمعير على المستعير كلام فاسد؛ لأن الواجب للمعير على المستعير هنا قيمة الثوب؛ ولو قال: "وجب" بدله لكان أولى.
If he borrows a garment to pawn it, it is valid. And if he specifies an amount or a type or a place, and he violates, then the lender may hold liable the lender? Actually 'المعير' is the lender. Commentary: The loan and pawn are valid because the lender voluntarily grants possession (yad) to the mortgagee, and this is compared to granting full ownership; possession can be separated from ownership, just as it separates in the case of a sale with option. Then the borrowed garment becomes a pawn for whatever it is pawned for, little or much, if the lender did not specify, because specification is required, especially in lending since ignorance does not lead to dispute. (al-'Aini, al-Fath) He holds the lender liable etc.: i.e., if the lender specifies the amount to pawn it for, or specifies the type, or specifies a place, and the borrower violates, the lender may choose to hold the borrower or the mortgagee liable; because both are transgressing; the borrower becomes like a usurper, and the mortgagee like the usurper's usurper. This is because the specification is meaningful, negating increase or decrease; if the borrower pawns for less than specified, the lender's purpose is thwarted; if for more, that also harms. Details from al-Dhakhira: if the garment's value equals the specified amount, and he pawns for less, he is liable for the value if the loss is less than the value? etc. Then if the lender holds the borrower liable, the pawn contract is completed between the borrower and the mortgagee because the borrower now owns the garment by paying compensation; if the lender holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee can claim from the borrower the amount paid and the debt from the pledgor. This is a summary. He becomes satisfied etc., because the mortgagee's possession is possession of satisfaction; by losing the garment, the debt is discharged from the pledgor, and he pays the lender its value, up to the amount of the debt; if the debt is fully covered, that is it; otherwise he pays the part that was guaranteed and the rest is a trust. And likewise if the value decreases due to a defect, the debt decreases proportionally. The author's statement 'wajaba mithlahu' is not apparent because the garment is a qimi (valuable) not mithli (fungible); Mulla Miskin's statement that the like of the debt is owed to the lender is corrupt; what is owed is the value of the garment. If he had said 'its substitute' it would be better.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage teaches the ruling on borrowing a garment (isti'arah) specifically for the purpose of pawning it (rahn). The base text states it is valid. The commentary explains the reasoning: the lender (mu'ir) voluntarily grants the mortgagee (murtahim) possession (yad) of the garment without transferring ownership. This is analogous (qiyas) to granting full ownership, as in a sale with an option (bai' bi al-khiyar), where possession transfers but ownership remains with the seller until the option is exercised. Thus, it is possible to separate possession from ownership. The borrowed garment becomes a valid pawn for whatever amount the borrower receives, whether little or much, if the lender did not specify a limit. The reason is that in a gratuitous loan (i'arah), uncertainty (jahala) does not lead to disputes because the borrower has no financial interest. However, if the lender specifies the amount, type of currency, or location of the pawn, and the borrower violates these conditions, the lender has a choice (khiyar) to either hold the borrower (musta'ir) or the mortgagee (murtahim) liable for the garment's value. Both are considered transgressors: the borrower violates the condition (like a usurper/ghasib), and the mortgagee accepts the pawn without the specified conditions (like the usurper of a usurper). The specification is meaningful because it protects the lender's interests: if the amount is too high, the borrower may struggle to repay; if too low, the lender might not recoup his loan if the pawn is lost. The text then gives a detailed rule from al-Dhakhira: if the specified amount equals the garment's value, and the borrower pawns for less, he is liable for the full value if the loss is less than the value? Actually it says three cases: (1) value equals specified amount: if he pawns for less, he guarantees the value; (2) value greater than specified amount: if he pawns for less or more than the specified but not exceeding value? The text is complex. The important takeaway is that the specification is treated like a condition; violating it incurs liability. If the borrower follows the specification exactly and the garment perishes with the mortgagee, the mortgagee's debt is satisfied (yastawfi) from the garment. Then the mortgagee must pay the lender the value of the garment up to the debt amount, and the remainder (if any) is a trust for the lender. Conversely, if the mortgagee holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee can then claim from the borrower both the compensation paid to the lender and the original debt from the pledgor. The commentator ends by critiquing a statement 'wajaba mithlahu' (its like is obligatory), insisting that the garment is a qimi (valuable, not fungible), so the compensation is its market value (qimah), not a like item.

Key Terms
استعارة (isti'arah): Borrowing for use; here specifically for pawning.
قيمي (qimi): A non-fungible item whose value varies; compensation is its market value.
قبض استيفاء (qabd istifa'): Possession that serves as satisfaction; here the mortgagee's possession is for collecting the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lender specifies that a borrowed garment be pawned for 100 dirhams, and the borrower pledges it for 100 dirhams but the garment is lost with the mortgagee, who is liable?
A) The borrower is liable for the garment's value
B) The mortgagee is liable for the garment's value
C) The debt is discharged, and the mortgagee must pay the lender the value of the garment up to 100 dirhams
D) No one is liable because the conditions were met

Key Takeaway
Borrowing a garment to pawn it is valid based on qiyas of possession; if the lender specifies conditions and the borrower violates, the lender has a choice to hold the borrower or mortgagee liable for the garment's market value.

Market Value Drop Does Not Reduce Pledge Debt
Hanafi ruling on pledgee's recourse when pledged slave's market value drops then is killed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on market value decrease of a pledged item after destruction, and explain the distinction between market value decrease and physical decrease.

Core Idea
Market value decrease does not reduce the pledge debt; only physical loss does.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a subtle but important ruling: when a pledged slave's market value drops and then the slave is killed, the pledgee receives the compensation and cannot claim the remaining debt from the pledgor. The reasoning hinges on distinguishing market fluctuations from true physical loss. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi pledge law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A slave worth 1000 is pledged for a 1000 debt. Its market value drops to 100, then a third party kills it and pays 100 as compensation.
Focus on the two changes: the drop in price and the destruction.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The pledgee receives the 100 as payment for the debt and does not recourse on the pledgor for the remaining 900.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the Reasoning
Market value decrease (nuqsan al-si'r) is not like physical decrease (nuqsan al-'ayn). Market decrease is a matter of public desire, not loss of substance. It does not reduce the debt. The pledgee's hand is a hand of satisfaction (yad istifa'), so the substitute (value at death) stands in for the original value.
Analogy: same rule applies in sale before possession and usurpation.
4
Compare with Zufar's View
Zufar equates market decrease with physical decrease, arguing that the debt should be reduced proportionally, allowing the pledgee to recourse for 900.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response rejects Zufar's analogy because market decrease does not affect the debt in other contexts. The teacher's refutation shows inconsistencies in Zufar's reported position.
The commentator clarifies that Zufar's actual view may not support recourse.

Source Text

الألف، وقال زفر لله يرجع بتسع مائة، وقال في "الفتح" بعد نقل كلام العيني المذكور والحاصل أن خلاف زفر ثابت في الشروح كالزيلعي وغيره انتهى، لكن ما ذكره في "ملا مسكين" من مذهب زفر وقرّره في "الفتح" محل The ruling on disposition in the pledge and injury upon it. (If) a slave worth one thousand is pledged for one thousand deferred, then its value falls to one hundred, and a man kills it, and he pays one hundred, and the term expires; the pledgor is liable for the slave erroneously? I guarantee the killer a dirham of the term? So the pledgee receives the one hundred as payment from his right, and does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything. And if he sells it, i.e., the debt term from the killer for the sake of payment for one hundred by his order, he receives the one hundred as payment from his right, the pledgor the pledgee the slave that was worth one thousand that invalidated the pledge because the debt falls by its destruction, and if he does not demand compensation for the injury, it remains a pledge as it was. And he does not recourse etc. because the decrease in price does not necessitate falling of the debt, so that he has the right to demand the entire debt when he returns it deficient in price, contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him. He says: The financial value has decreased, so it resembles decrease in the substance. And we say: Decrease in price is a matter of slackening of people's desires, and that is not considered in sale if it occurs in the sold item before possession, so the buyer does not get the option, nor in usurpation so that the usurper is not liable for what decreased in price when returning the usurped thing, unlike decrease in the substance because by the loss of a part thereof the satisfaction is determined. And when nothing of the debt fell due to decrease in price, it remains pledged for the entire debt. So if he kills it, he pays its value on the day of destruction and the pledgee takes it, because it is a substitute for the monetary value in the right of the entitled, even though it is comparable to blood according to our principle, so that it does not exceed the blood money of a free person. Then he does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything, because the pledgee's hand is a hand of satisfaction from the beginning, and by destruction it is determined, and its value was at the beginning one thousand, so he becomes satisfied with the entire amount from the beginning. And similar is in al-Takmila. I say: All the commentators of al-Kanz have mentioned the disagreement of Zufar, but they did not clarify its resolution except Mulla Miskin and al-Fath, where Mulla Miskin said: He does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything of the remaining thousand, and Zufar said: He recourses for nine hundred. And al-Fath said after quoting the aforementioned words of al-Ayni: The gist is that the disagreement of Zufar is established in the commentaries like al-Zaylai etc. end. But what Mulla Miskin mentioned of Zufar's doctrine and what he decided in al-Fath is questionable. Firstly, because the reasoning they mentioned from Zufar's side in the disagreement contradicts recourse upon the pledgor, for he equated decrease in price and decrease in the substance in falling of the debt, and it is apparent that in the case of decrease in the substance the pledgee does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything, so likewise in decrease in price. Secondly, because it is stated in al-Inayah that Zufar's doctrine in this case is that the pledgee does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything; for he said after mentioning: The issue here is three, and Zufar's statement that the ruling of the first and second pictures is one in that the pledgor ransoms it with its monetary value and the nine hundred falls from him by analogy to the second picture; for its ruling is that the nine hundred falls from the pledgor by agreement, and the pledgee has that hundred which the free man guaranteed at the expiration of the term. End. And the second picture is the issue of the book, so this statement clearly indicates this picture by agreement on the non-recourse upon the pledgor, and its interpretation as meaning the agreement of the Imam and his two companions, as done in al-Fath, is nothing, as is apparent. And the discussion can be expanded, but I suffice with this amount for notification.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi commentary on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq about a pledged slave whose market value drops from 1000 to 100 and then is killed by a man. The commentator explains that the pledgee (mortgagee) receives the 100 dirhams as payment for the debt and does not seek the remaining 900 from the pledgor. The reason is that market value decrease does not reduce the debt itself; the pledgor still owes the full amount. The pledgee's right is considered satisfied from the start because the value at the time of the pledge was 1000, and the substitute (the value paid by the killer) replaces that. The commentator contrasts this with the position of Zufar, who equates market decrease with physical decrease and would allow recourse. The Hanafi response distinguishes between loss of substance (which reduces the debt) and loss of market value (which does not). The commentator then discusses inconsistencies in reporting Zufar's view and defends the Hanafi position. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it follows the established madhhab.

Key Terms
نقصان السعر (nuqsan al-si'r): Decrease in market value, not a physical loss, but a fall in price due to market conditions.
يد استيفاء (yad istifa'): Hand of satisfaction; the pledgee's possession is for the purpose of collecting the debt, not for ownership.
استيفاء (istifa'): Receiving the full satisfaction of the debt; in this context, the pledgee is deemed to have received satisfaction from the beginning due to the substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a pledged slave's market value drops from 1000 to 100 and then the slave is killed, what is the pledgee's right regarding the remaining 900?
A) The pledgee can demand 900 from the pledgor.
B) The pledgee receives the 100 and cannot demand the remaining 900.
C) The pledgee must return the 100 to the killer.
D) The pledgee becomes owner of the killer's compensation and the debt is extinguished.

Key Takeaway
Market value decrease (nuqsan al-si'r) does not reduce the pledge debt; only physical decrease (nuqsan al-'ayn) does, and the pledgee's recourse is limited accordingly.

Sale of Pledged Slave by Pledgee with Pledgor's Permission
Hanafi ruling on pledgee selling value-reduced pledge with permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pledgee sells a pledged item with the pledgor's permission, and explain the pledgee's right to recourse for the remaining debt.

Core Idea
When the pledgee sells with permission, the sale cancels the pledge; the pledgee takes the price and recourses for the balance.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh of pledge (rahn) where the pledged item's value drops. The pledgee, with the pledgor's permission, sells the item. What happens to the debt? The ruling provides clarity on the pledgee's rights and the pledgor's remaining obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the pledgee selling the pledged item with the pledgor's permission. The ruling: the pledgee may keep the sale price as payment and recourse for the remainder.
2
Note the critical condition
The permission of the pledgor is essential. Without it, the sale is suspended until ratification.
This distinguishes the case from selling without permission.
3
Determine the consequences
The sale terminates the pledge. The pledgee receives the price and can sue for the remaining debt. The pledgor is liable for the balance.
The ruling ensures the pledgee does not lose the debt due to depreciation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage explains a separate ruling: if the pledgee sells the slave (now worth 100) with the pledgor's permission, the pledgee takes the 100 as payment and then recourses on the pledgor for the remaining 900. The reasoning is that the sale with permission is treated as if the pledgor himself sold it, so the pledge is canceled and the debt remains except for the amount collected. The pledgee's recourse is thus valid. This is straightforward and does not involve the dispute with Zufar.
