Substitute for a Pledged Slave: The Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Hanafi ruling on substitution when a pledged slave of reduced value is killed by a slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the substitution of a pledged slave and explain the reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar.

Core Idea
The substitute stands in place of the original; the pledgor must pay the full debt regardless of market value decline.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario in pledge (rahn) law: a pledged slave's value has dropped, and then it is killed by another slave. The killer is offered as a substitute. How does this affect the debt? The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that the substitute replaces the original in substance, so the full debt remains due. However, there are intra-madhhab variations that reveal important principles about guarantee, trust, and analogy. This lesson will unpack the ruling, its proofs, and the practical differences between the positions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage and identify the facts: a pledged slave originally worth 1000, whose value declines to 100, is killed by another slave worth 100. The killer slave is given as a substitute. What is the legal question?
The question is whether the substitute slav treats as a replacement for the original or as a new pledge for its own value.
2
State the Relied-upon Hanafi Position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), the pledgor must pay the full debt of 1000 to redeem the substitute. Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
The principle: 'al-badal qa'im maqam al-mubdal' (the substitute stands in place of the substituted). Market value fluctuations do not reduce the debt.
3
Present the Opposing Views
Identify the views of Muhammad (who gives an option) and Zufar (who says the substitute is a new pledge for only 100). Understand their bases.
Muhammad analogizes to a sold item killed before possession; Zufar emphasizes the pledgee's hand as a 'hand of satisfaction' and proportional reduction.
4
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the Hanafi response to each opposing view. To Zufar: the substitute is identical in flesh and blood, so no reduction. To Muhammad: the substance of the pledge (ayn al-rahn) is a trust, so transfer without consent is not permitted.
The key usul point: the pledge is an amanah (trust) in Hanafi, not property of the pledgee.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The practical difference: under the two's view, the pledgor must pay 1000 to redeem. Under Muhammad's option, he can hand over the substitute and owe nothing. Under Zufar, he would only need to pay 100.
The mufta bihi is the two's view, so in practice the full debt remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قتله عبد قيمته مائة، فدفع به افتكه بكل الدين، وإن مات العبد المرهون المرتمن على الراهن الراهن باع وصيه الرهن وقضى الدين، فإن لم يكن له وصي نصب له وصي، وأمر بـ بإذن المرتمن لقيامه مقامه الوصي ببيعه. ورجع إلخ: أي على الراهن؛ لأنه لما باعه بإذن الراهن صار كأن الراهن استرده وباعه بنفسه، ولو كان كذلك بطل الرهن وبقي الدين إلا بقدر ما استوفى فكذا هنا (فتح) وإن قتله عبد إلخ يعني إن قتل العبد المرهون عبد قيمته مائة والمسألة بحالها، فدفع العبد القاتل بدل العبد المقتول الذي نقص قيمته إلى المائة افتكه الراهن بكل الدين، وهو الألف التام عندهما، وعند محمد: هو بالخيار إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين وإن شاء سلم العبد المدفوع إلى المرتهن بدينه ولا شيء عليه غيره وعند زفر يصير رهنا بمائة؛ لأن يد المرتمن يد استيفاء، وقد تقرر بالهلاك إلا أنه أخلف بدلا بقدر العشر، فبقي الدين بقدره. ولمحمد: أن المرهون تغير في ضمان المرتمن فيخير كالمبيع إذا قتل قبل القبض والمغصوب إذا قتل في يد الغاصب، يخير المشتري والمغصوب منه، ولهما في مقابلة زفر أن العبد الثاني قائم مقام الأول لحما ودما، ولو كان الأول قائما، وانتقص السعر لا يسقط شيء من الدين عندنا؛ لما ذكرنا، فكذلك إذا قام المدفوع مكانه، وفي مقابلة محمد: أن التغير لم يظهر في نفس العبد لقيام الثاني مقام الأول لحما ودما كما ذكرناه مع زفر، وعين الرهن أمانة عندنا، فلا يجوز تمليكه من المرتمن بغير رضاه، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو تراجع سعر حتى صار يساوي مائة ثم قتله عبد يساوي مائة فدفع به. (ملتقطا)
And if a slave worth one hundred kills it, and he gives that slave as a substitute, he (the pledgor) may redeem it with the entire debt, and if the pledged slave dies, the pledgee (has a claim) on the pledgor, the pledgor (or) his guardian sells the pledge and pays the debt; if he has no guardian, a guardian is appointed for him, and he is ordered to sell it with the permission of the pledgee because he stands in his place. And he recourses etc.: i.e., upon the pledgor; because when he sold it with the pledgor's permission, it is as if the pledgor took it back and sold it himself, and if that were so, the pledge would be invalidated and the debt would remain except for what was collected, so here too (Fath). And if it is killed by a slave etc.: meaning if the pledged slave is killed by a slave worth one hundred, and the case is as it was, and he gives the killer slave as a substitute for the slain slave whose value decreased to one hundred, the pledgor may redeem it with the entire debt, which is the full thousand according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad: he has a choice: if he wishes he may redeem it with the entire debt, and if he wishes he may hand over the substitute slave to the pledgee for his debt and nothing else is upon him. And according to Zufar it becomes a pledge for one hundred, because the pledgee's hand is a hand of satisfaction, and it has been determined by destruction except that he left a substitute to the extent of a tenth, so the debt remains to that extent. And for Muhammad: the pledged item changed in the guarantee of the pledgee, so he has a choice, like the sold item if it is killed before possession and the usurped item if it is killed in the hand of the usurper – the buyer and the person from whom it was usurped have a choice. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue against Zufar that the second slave stands in place of the first in flesh and blood, and if the first had remained and the price decreased, nothing of the debt would fall according to us, as we mentioned, so likewise when the substitute takes its place. And against Muhammad: that the change did not appear in the slave itself because the second stands in place of the first in flesh and blood as we mentioned with Zufar, and the substance of the pledge is a trust according to us, so it is not permissible to transfer ownership to the pledgee without his consent. And upon this disagreement, if the price increases until it becomes worth one hundred and then a slave worth one hundred kills it and he gives that slave as a substitute. (From Multaqata)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario: the pledged slave's value has dropped to 100, and then it is killed by another slave worth 100. The killer slave is given as a substitute. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the pledgor must pay the full debt of 1000 to redeem the substitute and the original pledge. Muhammad adds an option: the pledgor may instead hand over the substitute slave to the pledgee as full satisfaction, owing nothing more. Zufar holds that the substitute becomes a new pledge for only 100, proportional to the value. The commentary explains the reasoning: the substitute stands in place of the original in substance, so market value decrease is irrelevant. The pledgee's hand is one of satisfaction, so the debt is not reduced. The difference with Muhammad is about whether the change in the pledge gives the pledgor a choice. This reflects a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Standing in place of; the substitute slave is considered the same as the original in legal effect.
عين الرهن (ayn al-rahn): The substance of the pledge; it remains a trust (amanah) with the pledgee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a pledged slave worth 100 (down from 1000) is killed by a slave worth 100, what must the pledgor do to redeem the substitute?
A) Pay 100 to the pledgee.
B) Pay 1000 to the pledgee.
C) Hand over the substitute and owe nothing.
D) Pay 900 to the pledgee.

Key Takeaway
The substitute stands in place of the original in substance, so the debt remains unchanged despite a drop in market value.
